Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

6 min
Wisdom of Legislating Qiyas
Explaining the rationale behind qiyas legislation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the wisdom behind the legislation of qiyas in the Hanafi school and identify its role in preventing disagreement in non-textual matters.

Core Idea
Qiyas is legislated to preserve unity and adherence to Sunnah when texts are silent.

This passage clarifies why qiyas is a legitimate source of law. It explains that without qiyas, Muslims would face confusion and disagreement over issues not explicitly addressed in the Qur'an and Sunnah. Understanding this wisdom is essential to appreciate the necessity of analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose
The text states that Allah legislated qiyas so that people would remain united and follow the Prophetic Sunnah.
This is the primary rationale: unity and Sunnah adherence.
2
Recognize the problem without qiyas
Without qiyas, people would disagree on non-textual matters (masāʾil ghayr manṣūṣah) and raise objections such as 'how are these matters to be acted upon?' and 'why did Allah not mention them?'
The text lists potential objections to highlight the need for qiyas.
3
Understand the Hanafi stance
This wisdom underpins the Hanafi acceptance of qiyas as a primary source of law, emphasizing its divine sanction rather than human innovation.
Note that even opponents of qiyas accept it in some form; the Hanafi position is grounded in this teleological reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قیاس کو مشروع کرنے کی حکمت: اللہ تعالی نے قیاس کو اس لئے مشروع کیا کہ لوگوں میں اتفاق رہے اور سنت نبوی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی اتباع کر سکیں کیونکہ اگر قیاس مشروع نہ ہوتا تو مسائل غیر منصوصہ میں لوگ اختلاف کرتے اور طرح طرح کے اعتراضات کرتے کہ آخر ان مسائل پر عمل کیسے کیا جائے ؟ اور ان کو اللہ تعالی نے کیوں ذکر نہیں کیا؟ وغیر ذالک۔
The wisdom of legislating qiyas: Allah legislated qiyas so that people would remain united and could follow the Prophetic Sunnah. Because if qiyas were not legislated, people would differ in non-textual matters and raise various objections, such as: how are these matters to be acted upon? And why did Allah not mention them? etc.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage states the wisdom (hikmah) behind the legislation of qiyas in Islamic law. The author explains that qiyas was permitted to prevent disagreement among Muslims in matters not explicitly addressed in the primary sources (Qur'an and Sunnah). Without qiyas, people would be left to their own opinions, leading to division and objections against the divine law. By allowing analogy, the Sharīʿah ensures that the Sunnah remains the guiding principle even in new cases, fulfilling the purpose of ikhtilāf prevention.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause (ʿillah).
مشروع (mashrūʿ): Legislated or sanctioned by the Sharīʿah.
مسائل غیر منصوصہ (masāʾil ghayr manṣūṣah): Legal issues not explicitly mentioned in the primary texts (Qur'an and Sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why was qiyas legislated according to this passage?
A) To create new laws independent of the Sunnah
B) To maintain unity and ensure following the Sunnah in non-textual issues
C) To allow scholars to exercise personal opinion freely
D) To replace the Qur'an and Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a divinely legislated tool to ensure unity and adherence to the Sunnah in matters not explicitly addressed by revelation.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Five Stages of Qiyas for a Mujtahid
Enumeration and explanation of the five stages of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five stages of qiyas, describe the progression from text to ruling, and apply these stages to a simple legal analogy scenario.

Core Idea
Qiyas requires a disciplined progression through five stages: text, linguistic meaning, legal meaning, 'illah, and application.

In this passage, the author outlines the method a mujtahid must follow when performing qiyas (analogical deduction). Rather than a single intuitive step, qiyas is a structured journey that begins with the explicit words of the primary sources and moves through layers of meaning and identification of effective cause. Understanding these stages is essential for correct legal derivation (istinbat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the first stage: starting from the textual words (alfaz al-nusus)
The mujtahid begins by focusing on the actual words of the Qur'an or Hadith that are relevant to the case.
This stage requires precise knowledge of the Arabic text and its recension.
2
Understand the linguistic meanings of those words
The mujtahid then turns to the apparent linguistic meanings (al-ma'ani al-lughawiyyah al-zahirah) of the text.
This involves lexical analysis and understanding the language as used by the Arabs.
3
Understand the legal (shar'i) meanings
From the linguistic meanings, the mujtahid moves to the meanings intended by the Lawgiver (al-ma'ani al-shar'iyyah).
These may differ from the linguistic meanings due to technical usage in the Shari'ah.
4
Identify the 'illah (effective cause) and its signs
Within the legal meanings, the mujtahid looks for signs (amarat, 'alamat) that indicate the 'illah that justifies analogy.
The 'illah is what connects the original case to the new case.
5
Apply the ruling to the new case (maqis) via the 'illah
Finally, the mujtahid uses the identified signs and 'illah to prove the same ruling for the new case.
This is the actual analogical extension (qiyas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجتہدین کیلئے قیاس کرنے میں منازل خمسہ قولہ وار او بمعالم العلم :۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے متن کی توضیح بیان کی ہے کہ معالم اعلم سے مراد وہ عمل ہیں جن کی وجہ سے قیاس کرنے والے لوگ حکم کو معلوم کرتے ہیں۔ اور معتبرین سے مراد قیاس کرنے والے لوگ ہیں۔ اور مسالک سے مراد فکر دوڑانے والی جگہیں ہیں۔ تو گویا ان کے سلوک کی ابتدا ء لفظ نص سے ہے۔ اس لیے پہلے وہ معانی لغویہ ظاہرہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوتے ہیں۔ وہاں سے معانی شرعیہ باطنیہ کی طرف منتقل ہوتے ہیں۔ تو ان معانی شرعیہ کے اندر ایسی علامات و نشانیاں پاتے ہیں۔ جن کو شارع نے ودیعت کیا ہے تا کہ وہ قاکسین ان علتوں سے اپنے مقصود کی طرف راہ پاسکیں۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے قائسین کے لیے اس راستہ میں پانچ منزلیں ہیں۔ ۱۔ الفاظ نصوص ۔۲۔ ان الفاظ کے معانی لغویہ کومعلوم کرنا ۳۔ ان کے معانی شرعیہ کو معلوم کرنا ہے ۔ ۴۔ علل و امارات و علامات کو معلوم کرنا ۔۵۔ ان علامات کے ذریعے مقیس کے اندر حکم کو ثابت کرنا۔ قولہ ولما قال: اس عبارت میں مصنف نے متن کی خوبی کو بیان کیا ہے۔ کہ جب ماتن نے کہا۔ بنی علی اربعہ ارکان قصر الاحکام تو مصنف نے ارکان کو اسی ترتیب پر رکھ دیا۔ جس ترتیب کا شرعیت نے اعتبار کیا ہے۔ یعنی پہلے کتاب اللہ پھر سنت رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پھر اجماع پھر قیاس کو ذکر کیا ہے۔
Five stages for mujtahids in performing qiyas. His statement: 'warada bi ma'alim al-ilm': In this phrase the author explained the text: by 'ma'alim al-ilm' is meant the actions by which those performing qiyas come to know the ruling. By 'mu'tabirin' is meant those who perform qiyas. By 'masalik' is meant the paths of thought. So the beginning of their course is from the word of the nass. Therefore first they turn to the apparent linguistic meanings. From there they move to the inner legal meanings. Then within these legal meanings they find signs and indicators that the Lawgiver has deposited so that those performing qiyas may find their way to the intended goal by means of these 'illahs. Summary: For those performing qiyas, there are five stages: 1. The words of the nusus, 2. Knowing the linguistic meanings of these words, 3. Knowing their legal meanings, 4. Knowing the 'illahs, indications, and signs, 5. Through these signs proving the ruling in the maqis (subject of analogy). His statement: 'wa lamma qala': In this phrase the author explained the merit of the text. When the matan said 'It is built on four pillars: the pillars of ahkam', the author arranged the pillars in the order that the Shari'ah considered, i.e., first the Book of Allah, then the Sunnah of the Messenger, then ijma', then qiyas.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage enumerates the five stages (manazil) that a mujtahid goes through when performing qiyas. Starting with the literal texts, the mujtahid moves to linguistic meanings, then to legal meanings, then identifies the 'illah (effective cause) and its signs, and finally applies the ruling to the new case. The author also notes the virtue of the matn in ordering the four sources correctly.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): analogical deduction in legal reasoning
منازل خمسہ (manazil khamsah): five stages in the process of qiyas for a mujtahid
علت (illah): effective cause that justifies legal analogy
مقیس (maqis): the new case being analogically deduced

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first stage (manzil) in the process of qiyas according to this passage?
A) Knowing the 'illah of the original case.
B) The words of the nusus (texts).
C) Applying the ruling to the new case.
D) Understanding the legal meanings.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a multi-stage process that begins with the primary texts and proceeds through linguistic and legal analysis to identify the 'illah and apply the ruling.

Implicit Reference to Qiyas in Hanafi Usul Texts
Explanation of implicit inclusion of Qiyas via derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify implicit references to qiyas in Hanafi usul texts through derivational analysis of terms like 'mu'tabarīn'.

Core Idea
The Hanafi usul text implies Qiyas via 'mu'tabarīn'—derived from 'i'tibār', meaning analogy.

In this passage, the commentator highlights the virtue of the matn in ordering the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) following the Shari'ah. He also answers a key question: why does the matn only explicitly mention three proofs? The answer lies in the term 'mu'tabarīn', which indirectly invokes qiyas. Understanding this derivational inference is essential for reading Hanafi usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's explicit sources
List the three proofs the matn explicitly mentions: Kitab (Quran), Sunnah, and Ijma. Note that Qiyas is not directly named.
This sets up the puzzle the commentator will solve.
2
Locate the implicit source
Find the phrase 'mu'tabarīn' in the matn. Recognize that this term is derived from the Arabic root 'i'tibār'.
The commentator uses this term to answer the implied question.
3
Perform linguistic derivation
Show that 'i'tibār' means reflection and analogy in Arabic. The Arabs say 'i'tabartu al-shay' when they ponder something. Thus, 'mu'tabarīn' refers to those who perform qiyas.
Hanafi usul often relies on such derivational clues to include qiyas.
4
Understand the commentator's method
The commentator argues that the matn implicitly includes Qiyas through this derivational cue, thereby maintaining the four-source structure.
5
Apply the lesson
Recognize similar implicit references in other Hanafi texts, e.g., 'ahl al-ra'y', 'ashab al-qiyas', or 'al-i'tibār'.
This skill helps in identifying all four sources even when not explicitly enumerated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذکرھا: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شارح نے متن کی خوبی بیان کی ہے۔ کہ جس طرح ترتیب کے ساتھ شرعیت نے ارکان اربعہ کو رکھا ہے۔ پہلے نمبر پر کتاب اللہ پھر سنت رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پھر اجماع پھر قیاس کو، اسی طرح ماتن نے بھی ارکان اربعہ کو اسی ترتیب پر ذکر کیا ہے۔ ذکر الثلاثہ: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شارح نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال: ماتن نے دلائل ثلاثہ (کتاب اللہ سنت رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اور اجماع) کو تو اپنی کتاب میں ذکر کیا لیکن قیاس کا کہیں بھی ذکر نہیں کیا۔ جواب: پہلے تین دلائل کا صراحتہ ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور قیاس کو اپنے قول «وضع معالم العلم علی مسالک المعتبرین» میں ضمنا ذکر کیا۔ کیونکہ معتبرین مشتق ہے۔ فاعتبرو او اولی الابصار سے بمعنی اے منظمند و قیاس کرو اس لیے کہ اہل عرب کہتے ہیں اعتبرت الشئی یعنی جب تو کسی شی میں غور و فکر کرے تو معتبرین سے مراد قیاس کرنے والے لوگ ہوں گے۔ حکم اس اثر کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ذریعہ قیاس پر استدلال کیا جائے۔ مراد اس سے حکم کی علت ہے۔
Then He Mentioned Them: This is the fifth part of the commentary's phrase. In this phrase the commentator explained the virtue of the text: that just as the Shari'ah arranged the four pillars in order — first the Book of Allah, then the Sunnah of the Messenger, then consensus, then analogy — similarly the author also mentioned the four pillars in that order. Mention of the Three: This is the sixth part of the commentary's phrase. In this phrase the commentator answered an implied question. Question: The author mentioned the three proofs (Book, Sunnah, Ijma) in his book but did not mention Qiyas anywhere. Answer: He explicitly mentioned the first three proofs, and implied Qiyas in his statement: 'He placed the landmarks of knowledge upon the paths of those who are considered (mu'tabarīn).' Because mu'tabarīn is derived from 'i'tibār' meaning reflection and analogy. The Arabs say 'i'tabartu al-shay' when you ponder over something. So mu'tabarīn refers to those who perform qiyas. 'Hukm' here means the effect by which qiyas is argued, i.e., the 'illah of the ruling.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage consists of two parts. First, the commentator highlights the virtue of the matn in following the established order of evidence: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. This order reflects the hierarchical strength and sequence of derivation. Second, the commentator addresses why the matn explicitly mentions only three proofs but not Qiyas. The answer is that Qiyas is implicitly included in the phrase 'upon the paths of those who are considered (mu'tabarīn)', which derives from the root 'i'tibār', meaning to ponder or analogize. Thus Qiyas is part of the methodology. The term 'hukm' in this context refers to the 'illah (effective cause) that is the basis of analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
معتبرین (mu'tabarīn): Those who perform i'tibar (reflection/analogy), used to indicate practitioners of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the commentator argue that the matn implicitly includes Qiyas as one of the four sources?
A) By a later addition in the margin.
B) By the phrase 'upon the paths of those who are considered (mu'tabarīn)' which derives from a root meaning analogy.
C) By saying 'Qiyas' in a different part of the text.
D) By referring to Ijma as including Qiyas.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas can be implicitly included through derivational terms like 'mu'tabarīn', reflecting the school's reliance on linguistic inference.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Role of Qiyas in Hanafi Usul: Manifestor, Not Establisher
Refutation of objection from comprehensiveness of hukm definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qiyas does not establish new rulings but manifests the applicability of the divine address, and evaluate the objection that rulings from qiyas are excluded from the definition of hukm.

Core Idea
Qiyas manifests the divine address; it does not create new rulings.

This passage presents the third objection to the Ash'ari definition of hukm (the address of Allah related to acts of the mukallaf). The objector argues that rulings established by qiyas are excluded from this definition, yet they are valid rulings. The Hanafi response provides a crucial clarification: qiyas does not create rulings; it only reveals that the divine address already covers the analogous case. We will walk through the objection, the response, and the syntactic analysis that anchors this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Find the claim: the Ash'ari definition of hukm excludes rulings established by qiyas because they are not directly from Allah's address.
The objector assumes qiyas creates new rulings independent of divine address.
2
Examine the Hanafi Response
The response denies that qiyas establishes rulings. It states that qiyas is a 'muzhir' (manifestor) of the ruling, not a 'muthbit' (establisher). The divine address in the original case is shown to apply to the analogue.
Key Arabic: القياس مظہر حکم ہے نہ کہ مثبت حکم
3
Analyze the Syntactic Argument
The commentator explains that the exception phrase 'illa an yuqal' (unless it is said) can be interpreted as an adverb of time, excepting the time when the response is given. This preserves the definition's comprehensiveness.
The phrase 'الا ان یقال' is treated as a time adverb, narrowing the exception.
4
Derive the Usul Principle
From this passage, derive the principle: qiyas is a method of manifesting (izhar) that the divine ruling applies to a new case, not a source of new law.
This is foundational for understanding the Hanafi approach to qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخرج منہ ما ثبت بالقیاس:۔ يہاں سے تیسرا اعتراض نقل فرمایا ہے۔ اعتراض (۳):۔ اشاعرہ نے حکم کی تعریف جو کی ہے یہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے وہ حکم نکل جاتا ہے جو قیاس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ خطاب اللہ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا حالانکہ وہ بھی حکم ہی ہوتا ہے الا ان یقال یدرک بالقياس ...
يہاں سے جواب دیا ہے۔
جواب:۔ آپ کا اعتراض تو تب درست ہے کہ جب قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہو حالانکہ قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قیاس سے تو یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مقیس میں بھی خطاب اللہ وارد ہوا ہے یعنی قیاس سے خطاب اللہ کے مقیس میں وارد ہونے کا اظہار ہوتا ہے نئے سرے سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ قیاس مظہر حکم ہے نہ کہ مثبت حکم لہذا آپ کا اعتراض درست نہیں۔
ترکیبی تحقیق
اعلم ان المصادر قد بلغ ظرفاً: ۔ يہاں سے ماتن نے الا ان یقال کی ترکیبی تحقیق بیان کی ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ کبھی کبھی مصدر ظرف واقع ہوتا ہے اور وقت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے جیسے آتیک طلوع الشمس ای وقت طلوع الشمس اسی طرح الا ان یقاں ہے کیونکہ جب ان مصدر یہ فعل پر داخل ہوتا ہے تو یہ اس کو مصدر کی تاویل میں کر دیتا ہے تو گویا ان یقال قول کے معنی میں ہے اور ظرف واقع ہورہا ہے تو یہ وقت کے معنی پر مشتمل ہوگا اور کیونکہ یہ متمنی مفرغ ہے (اس کا مستثنی منہ مذکور نہیں ) اور وہ
ہے فی جمیع الاوقات تو اب معنیٰ ہوگا ، يخرج منہ ما ثبت بالقياس في جميع الاوقات الا وقت قولہ یدرک بالقیاس یعنی حکم کی تعریف سے ثابت بالقیاس خارج ہو گا مگر جس وقت اس کے جواب میں کہا جائے کہ قیاس مظہر احکام ہے مثبت احکام نہیں۔
There emerges from it that which is established by qiyas. Here the third objection is narrated. Objection (3): The definition of hukm given by the Ash'aris is not comprehensive because it excludes the ruling that is established by qiyas, since it is not established by the address of Allah, even though it is also a ruling, unless it is said that it is known by qiyas... Here the answer is given. Answer: Your objection would be correct only if a ruling is established by qiyas, but a ruling is not established by qiyas. Rather, through qiyas it is known that the address of Allah has occurred in the analogue, i.e., qiyas manifests the occurrence of the address of Allah in the analogue; it does not establish a new ruling. Because qiyas is a manifestation of the ruling, not an establisher of the ruling. Therefore your objection is not correct. Syntactic investigation: Know that the verbal nouns sometimes occur as adverbs of time, as in 'I come to you at the rising of the sun' meaning 'at the time of the sunrise'. Similarly, 'illa an yuqal' because when 'an' (that) enters upon a verb, it turns it into a verbal noun. So 'an yuqal' is in the meaning of 'qawl' (saying), and it occurs as an adverb, thus it signifies a time. And since it is a 'mutammana mufarrag' (its excepted-from is not mentioned), and it is in all times, the meaning becomes: 'There emerges from it that which is established by qiyas in all times except the time when it is said in response that qiyas is a manifestation of rulings, not an establisher of rulings.'
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection (اعتراض) to the Ash'ari definition of hukm (judgment) as 'the address of Allah related to the acts of the legally responsible' and its response. The objector argues that the definition excludes rulings established through qiyas (analogy), because such rulings are not directly from Allah's address, yet they are considered rulings. The response clarifies that qiyas does not create rulings; it merely reveals that the divine address encompasses the analogue. Thus the definition remains comprehensive. The commentator then provides a syntactic analysis (الترکیبی تحقیق) of the phrase 'الا ان یقال' (unless it is said), explaining that the verbal noun 'ان یقال' can function as an adverb of time, meaning 'except the time when it is said'. This demonstrates that the exception applies specifically to the time of the counterargument. Hence, the definition is preserved.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): A method of legal reasoning that manifests (izhar) that the divine address applies to the analogue; it is not a source that establishes a new ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Qiyas as Muzhir: Rulings Derived by Analogy Are Part of Allah's Address
Third objection against a definition of hukm and its rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ruling derived by qiyas are considered part of Allah's address according to Hanafi usul, and distinguish between qiyas as muzhir (revealer) vs muthbit (establisher).

Core Idea
Qiyas does not create new rulings; it reveals Allah's address already implicit in the sources.

This passage presents the third objection against a definition of hukm that restricts it to the direct address of Allah. The objection claims that rulings derived by qiyas (analogical deduction) are excluded because qiyas involves human reasoning, not a divine address. The response is a fundamental principle of Hanafi usul: qiyas is a 'revealer' (muzhir) of the ruling, not an 'establisher' (muthbit). It uncovers what is already contained in the divine texts. The same reasoning applies to Sunnah and Ijma: all proofs (adillah) are disclosers of Allah's address, not independent sources.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Identify the claim: the definition of hukm being critiqued does not include rulings derived by qiyas because qiyas lacks a direct divine address (khitab Allah). Reason: qiyas is human reasoning, not revelation.
2
Analyze the Response: Muzhir vs Muthbit
The response uses a crucial distinction: qiyas is a 'revealer' (muzhir) of the ruling, not an 'establisher' (muthbit). That means qiyas does not create a new ruling from nothing; it uncovers what the divine address already implies. This preserves the idea that all rulings ultimately come from Allah.
Muzhir: revealer; Muthbit: establisher
3
Extend to Sunnah and Ijma
The text notes that the same objection could be raised against rulings from Sunnah and Ijma (since they also are not direct divine addresses). The response applies uniformly: each of these sources is a 'discloser' (kashif) and 'manifestor' (mu'arrif) of Allah's address. That is the meaning of calling them 'proofs of rulings' (adillat al-ahkam).
All four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) serve as indicators (adillah) that reveal the same divine address.
4
Synthesize the Hanafi Position
Consolidate the lesson: In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a valid source of law because it reveals the divine ruling. It is not an independent source of legislation but a method of discovery. The ruling derived by qiyas is genuinely from Allah, though the process of discovery uses human reasoning.
This preserves the Quranic principle that 'ruling is only for Allah' (al-hukmu illa lillah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثَّالِثُ أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ غَيْرُ مُتَنَاوِلٍ لِلْحُكُمِ الثَّابِتِ بِالْقِيَاسِ لِعَدَمِ خِطَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَأَجَابَ بِأَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ مُظهِرٌ لِلْحُكُم لَا مُثبت وَلَا يَخْفَى عَلَيْكَ أَنَّ السُّوَالَ وَارِدٌ فِيمَا ثَبَتَ بِالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ أَيْضًا وَالْجَوَابُ أَنْ كُلَّا مِنْهُمَا كَاشِفَ عَنْ خِطَابِ اللَّهِ وَمُعَرّت لَهُ ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى كَوْنِهَا أَدِلَّةَ الْأَحْكَامِ
The third [objection]: that the definition does not include the ruling established by qiyas because there is no address of Allah the Exalted [in qiyas]. And he answered that qiyas is a revealer of the ruling, not an establisher. And it is not hidden from you that the question also applies to what is established by the Sunnah and Ijma, and the answer is that each of them is a discloser of Allah's address and a manifestor of it, and this is the meaning of them being proofs of rulings.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This is the third objection against a particular definition of hukm (likely the one that restricts hukm to the direct address of Allah). The objection states that rulings derived by qiyas (analogical deduction) are not covered because qiyas involves human reasoning, not a direct divine address. The response is that qiyas does not establish a new ruling ex nihilo; it merely reveals what is already contained in the divine address. Similarly, the objection is extended to rulings from Sunnah (prophetic tradition) and Ijma (consensus), which also are not direct addresses from Allah in the same sense. The response for all three is that they are all 'disclosers' (kashif) and 'manifestors' (mu'arrif) of Allah's address, not independent sources. This is the meaning of calling them 'proofs of rulings' (adillat al-ahkam).

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; a method of deriving a ruling by comparing a new case with an original case that has a clear textual ruling.
مظهر (muzhir): Revealer; qiyas is said to be a revealer of the ruling, not an establisher.
مثبت (muthbit): Establisher; qiyas is denied this role.
أدلة الأحكام (adillat al-ahkam): The proofs of rulings: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) By saying qiyas is an establisher of a new ruling.
C) By saying qiyas is a revealer of the ruling, not an establisher.
D) By saying qiyas has no connection to Allah's address.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas reveals the divine address; it does not establish new rulings independent of it.

Qiyas: Manifestor of Divine Ruling, Not Producer
Ash'ari objection and Hanafi response on qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that qiyas is a manifestor (muzhir) rather than a producer (muthbit) of rulings, and evaluate the Ash'ari objection that the definition of fiqh excludes qiyas-derived rulings.

Core Idea
Qiyas does not create new rulings; it only manifests the divine address already present in the original case.

The Ash'aris defined fiqh as knowledge of Allah's rulings from detailed evidences, taking 'hukm' as direct divine address. They objected that this definition excludes rulings derived by qiyas, since qiyas is not direct address. In response, the Hanafis clarify that qiyas does not produce a new ruling; it only manifests the existing ruling from the original to the analogous case. This distinction preserves the comprehensiveness of the definition and reflects the Hanafi view that all rulings are ultimately from divine address.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari objection
The Ash'aris define fiqh as knowledge of rulings from detailed evidences, where 'hukm' is the address of Allah. They argue that rulings established by qiyas are not directly from that address, so they would be excluded, making the definition incomplete.
The objection is that the definition fails to encompass all valid rulings.
2
Understand the Hanafi rejection
The Hanafis deny that qiyas establishes a new ruling. Instead, qiyas only manifests the ruling of the original case in the new case through a shared effective cause (illa). The ruling is still essentially from divine address.
Key: qiyas is a method of discovery, not creation.
3
Analyze key terms: muthbit vs muzhir
Muthbit (producer) implies bringing a ruling into existence. Muzhir (manifestor) means revealing or uncovering what already exists. Hanafis use the latter to describe qiyas.
This semantic distinction carries significant legal implications.
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the Hanafi view, all rulings—whether directly from texts or via qiyas—are considered part of divine address, so the definition of fiqh remains comprehensive. This also affects how ijtihad is understood.
The scope of 'hukm' in definitions of fiqh is at stake.
5
Evaluate both positions
Compare the coherence of each view. The Hanafi position aligns with the idea that the law is complete and ijtihad uncovers it. The Ash'ari position treats qiyas as a creative source, potentially widening the scope of new rulings.
Which view better preserves the principle that all rulings come from Allah?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث ان التعریف: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ ماتن کی جانب سے اشاعرہ پر ہونے والے تیسرے اعتراض اور اسکے جواب کی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں۔ اعتراض (۳): اشاعرہ نے جو فقہ کی تعریف کی ہے وہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے وہ احکام نکل جاتے ہیں جو قیاس سے ثابت ہیں کیونکہ تعریف میں حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ الخ لیا گیا ہے اور قیاس خطاب الله .. الخ نہیں اس لئے قیاس سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام تعریف سے خارج ہو گئے لہذ ا تعریف جامع نہ رہی ۔ واجاب بان القیاس۔ یہاں سے جواب کی وضاحت ہے ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہی نہیں کہ قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ قیاس حکم کے لئے مثبت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مظہر ہوتا ہے یعنی قیاس کے ذریعہ کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ قیاس کے ذریعہ یہ ظاہر کیا جاتا ہے کہ فلاں حکم (مقیس ) میں خطاب اللہ وارد ہوا ہے تو جب قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہی نہیں ہوتا تو آپ کا اعتراض بھی درست نہ ہو لہذ اہماری تعریف جامع ہے۔
The third [point] is that the definition [of fiqh by Ash'aris] is not comprehensive because it excludes rulings established by qiyas, since in the definition, 'hukm' is taken to mean 'address of Allah', and qiyas is not an address of Allah. Therefore, rulings from qiyas are excluded, so the definition is not comprehensive. Response: We do not agree that qiyas establishes a ruling. Qiyas is not a producer (muthbit) of a ruling but a manifestor (muzhir). That is, qiyas does not establish a ruling but rather manifests that in the analogous case (maqis) the address of Allah has been revealed. Since qiyas does not establish a ruling, the objection is invalid, and our definition is comprehensive.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage presents an Ash'ari objection to a particular definition of fiqh, arguing that rulings derived by qiyas (analogy) are not covered by the definition if it only includes direct divine address. The Hanafi response is that qiyas does not create new rulings; it only reveals or manifests rulings that already exist in the divine address. In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a method of discovering the law, not creating it. Therefore, all rulings, whether directly from texts or via qiyas, are ultimately from divine address, so the definition remains comprehensive. This reflects the Hanafi position that qiyas is a valid source only as a means of manifesting the hukm already present in the sources.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; here, a manifestor of ruling
مثبت (muthbit): Producer or establisher of a ruling
مظہر (muzhir): Manifestor or revealer of a ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas does not create new rulings; it only manifests the existing divine address, thereby preserving the comprehensiveness of definitions of fiqh.

Qiyas as Mazhir Not Muthbit – The Hanafi Response
Third objection by Asha'ira on definition excluding qiyas and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi view that qiyas is mazhir from the Ash'ari view that it is muthbit, and evaluate the impact on the definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
Qiyas reveals Allah's ruling; it does not create a new one.

The Ash'ari definition of fiqh as knowledge of Allah's direct address would exclude rulings derived from qiyas, since qiyas is not a direct address. In response, Hanafi scholars argue that qiyas is not an independent source but a revealer (mazhir) of rulings already implicit in revelation. This lesson unpacks the logic behind that response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari objection
The Ash'ari definition of fiqh defines it as knowledge of Allah's legal rulings derived from detailed evidence, where 'hukm' refers directly to Allah's address. The objector argues that rulings from qiyas are excluded because qiyas is not Allah's address.
2
State the Hanafi counter-claim
The Hanafi response does not accept that qiyas establishes a new ruling. Instead, it claims qiyas is mazhir (revealer) not muthbit (establisher).
3
Understand the mazhir vs muthbit distinction
A muthbit brings a new ruling into existence independent of revelation. A mazhir makes evident a ruling that is already present in revelation. The Hanafis hold that qiyas only manifests a ruling already covered by divine address through the original case (asl) and common cause (illah).
This is a core usul principle distinguishing the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to the definition
Since qiyas does not create but reveals, rulings derived from qiyas are still part of Allah's address, so the Ash'ari definition remains comprehensive and the objection is invalid.
Thus the definition is saved from the criticism of being non-comprehensive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث ان التعریف:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارح ماتن کی جانب سے اشاعرہ پر ہونے والے تیسرے اعتراض اور اسکے جواب کی وضاحت کر رہے ہیں۔
اعتراض (۳): اشاعرہ نے جو فقہ کی تعریف کی ہے وہ جامع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس سے وہ احکام نکل جاتے ہیں جو قیاس سے ثابت ہیں کیونکہ تعریف میں حکم سے مراد خطاب اللہ الخ لیا گیا ہے اور قیاس خطاب الله .. الخ نہیں اس لئے قیاس سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام تعریف سے خارج ہو گئے لہذا تعریف جامع نہ رہی۔
واجاب بان القیاس۔ یہاں سے جواب کی وضاحت ہے ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہی نہیں کہ قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ قیاس حکم کے لئے مثبت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مظہر ہوتا ہے یعنی قیاس کے ذریعہ کوئی حکم ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ قیاس کے ذریعہ یہ ظاہر کیا جاتا ہے کہ فلاں حکم (مقیس ) میں خطاب اللہ وارد ہوا ہے تو جب قیاس سے کوئی حکم ثابت ہی نہیں ہوتا تو آپ کا اعتراض بھی درست نہ ہو لہذا ہماری تعریف جامع ہے۔
The third [point] concerning the definition: This is the seventh part of the commentary's text. From here, the commentator explains the third objection against the Asha'ira and its response.
Objection (3): The definition of fiqh given by the Asha'ira is not comprehensive because it excludes rulings established by qiyas. Since in the definition, 'hukm' refers to the address of Allah, and qiyas is not the address of Allah, rulings derived from qiyas are excluded from the definition, so the definition is not comprehensive.
And he answered about qiyas. From here is the explanation of the response: We do not accept that a ruling is established by qiyas, because qiyas is not a positive establisher of a ruling but a revealer. That is, by qiyas a ruling is not established; rather, by qiyas it is made evident that the address of Allah has occurred concerning that ruling (the maqis). So when no ruling is established by qiyas, your objection is invalid, and thus our definition is comprehensive.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute between the Hanafis and the Ash'ari school (Asha'ira) regarding the definition of fiqh. The Ash'ari definition defines fiqh as knowledge of Allah's legal rulings derived from detailed evidence. The objector (apparently the matn's author) argues that this definition excludes rulings derived from qiyas because qiyas is not a direct address of Allah. The Hanafi response is that qiyas does not establish a new ruling; rather, it reveals that Allah's address has already covered the case. Thus, rulings from qiyas are not excluded because they are essentially manifestations of existing revelation. This distinction between muthbit (establisher) and mazhir (revealer) is key to the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic jurisprudence; a method to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause.
مظہر (mazhir): Revealer or manifestor; something that shows or makes evident a ruling that already exists in revelation.
مثبت (muthbit): Establisher or positer; something that brings a new ruling into existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It establishes new rulings independently
B) It reveals existing rulings from revelation
C) It is not a valid source of law
D) It only applies to fard rulings

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a revealer of existing divine rulings, not a creator of new ones; thus, it does not exclude rulings from the definition of fiqh.

Qiyasi Issues and the Problem of Circularity in Defining Fiqh
Explaining why qiyasi issues are excluded from fiqh definition to avoid dawr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical problem of dawr in defining fiqh and explain why qiyasi issues are excluded, and evaluate the objection that later mujtahids can avoid circularity by taqlid.

Core Idea
Including qiyasi issues in the definition of fiqh creates a circular dependency (dawr), which is logically invalid.

This passage from a commentary on al-Taftazani's work addresses a subtle but crucial point in usul al-fiqh: the proper scope of the definition of fiqh. Understanding why analogical rulings are excluded prevents a logical fallacy and sharpens your grasp of what fiqh truly is. The passage presents a dispute over whether later mujtahids can rely on earlier derivations without causing circularity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The passage begins by asserting that qiyasi issues are not part of the definition of fiqh. Determine the exact phrasing and the reason given.
The claim is that including them would lead to dawr.
2
Understand the logical problem of dawr
Trace the argument: fiqh consists of rulings; qiyasi issues are rulings derived through ijtihad; if they are part of fiqh, then understanding fiqh depends on them, but they depend on ijtihad, which is itself part of fiqh. This creates a circular dependency.
Dawr is a well-recognized defect in definitions.
3
Examine the objection
The objector argues that dawr only applies to the first mujtahid, not to later ones, because they can rely on the first mujtahid's qiyasi issues without deriving them themselves.
This is plausible if taqlid were allowed for mujtahids.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response (Qulna) rejects the objection: a mujtahid cannot perform taqlid. The later mujtahid must independently derive qiyasi issues, thus the same circularity recurs for him.
This upholds the principle that mujtahids must exert ijtihad.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether knowledge of qiyasi rulings is required for a jurist to be considered a faqih. The Hanafi position says no, to avoid dawr; the objector would say yes for later mujtahids.
This clarifies the boundaries of the definition of fiqh.

تشریح مسائل قیاسیہ کا علم فقہ کی تعریف میں شرط نہیں قولہ لا المسائل القیاسیہ: یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض تفتازانی توضیح متن ہے کہ فقہ کے لئے مسائل قیاسیہ کا جاننا ضروری نہیں کیونکہ ایسی صورت میں دور لازم آئے گا وہ ایسے کہ فقیہ کی فقاہت پر مسائل قیاسیہ کا سمجھنا موقوف ہے اس لئے کہ سائل قیاسیہ اجتہاد سے مستقبط شدہ فروع کا نام ہے تو جب تک فقیہ میں فقاہت اور اجتہاد کی صلاحیت نہیں ہوگی ان مسائل کا استنباط بھی نہیں ہو گا۔ اب اگر فقہ کی تعریف میں مسائل قیاسیہ داخل ہوں تو فقہ کا سمجھنا موقوف ہو گا مسائل قیاسیہ پر کیونکہ کل کا وجود موقوف ہے اس کے اجزاء پر تو فقاہت خود فقاہت پر موقوف ہوگی مسائل قیاسیہ کے واسطے سے کیونکہ شئی کے موقوف عالیہ کا موقوف علیہ کی کا موقوف علیہ ہوتا ہے لہذا یہ توقف الشئی علی نفسہ ہے اور دور ہے اور دور باطل ہے تومستلزم دور بھی باطل ہے۔ فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض اعتراض کو نقل کرتا ہے۔ اعتراض: فقیہ اول پر تو یہ دور والی خرابی لازم آتی ہے کیونکہ مجتہد اول نے ان مسائل قیاسیہ کا خود استنباط کیا ہے اب اگر اس کے لئے ان مسائل کا جاننا ضروری ہو تو دور لازم آئے گا کیونکہ وہ اس فقیہ اول کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ ہیں لیکن اگر بعد میں آنے والے مجتہدین کے لئے پہلے والے مجتہد کے مستقبط شدہ قیاسی مسائل کا جاننا ضروری ہو تو اس سے دور لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ یہ مسائل پہلے فقیہ کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ ہیں دوسرے کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ نہیں جب دوسرے فقیہ کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ نہیں تو یہ فقیہ ثانی کی فقاہت پر موقوف نہ ہوئے اب فقاہت تو موقوف ہوگی مسائل قیاسیہ پر لیکن مسائل قیاسیہ مجتہد اول کی فقاہت پر موقوف ہوں گے نہ کہ فقیہ ثانی کی فقاہت پر تو دور لازم نہیں آئے گا۔ جواب: قلنا یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض اسی سوال کا جواب ہے کہ دوسرے مجتہد کے لئے بھی دور لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ مجتہد کے لئے تقلید جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ فقیہ ثانی ان مسائل میں بھی خود اجتہاد کرے گا جب اجتہاد کے ذریعے جانے گا تو اس کی فقاہت ان مسائل قیاسیہ پر موقوف ہوگی اور مسائل قیاسیہ اسکے اجتہاد کی وجہ سے فقاہت پر موقوف ہو نگے یہ دور نہیں تو اور کیا ہے۔ تم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض ایک فائدہ کا بیان ہے دوسرے مجتہد کے لئے پہلے مجتہد کے اقوال کا
Explanation: Knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in the definition of fiqh. His statement: 'not the qiyasi issues': This is the first part of the phrase; its purpose is that Taftazani explains the matn: that knowing qiyasi issues is not necessary for fiqh, because if it were, circularity would occur. That is, a jurist's juristic ability (fiqaha) is dependent on understanding qiyasi issues because qiyasi issues are branches derived through ijtihad. As long as the jurist does not have the capacity for juristic ability and ijtihad, deriving these issues is not possible. Now if qiyasi issues are included in the definition of fiqh, then understanding fiqh would be dependent on qiyasi issues, because the existence of the whole depends on its parts. Then juristic ability itself would be dependent on itself through qiyasi issues, because something's high dependent's dependent is a dependent, so this is a thing depending on itself, which is circularity (dawr), and circularity is invalid. So what entails circularity is also invalid. 'Fain qeel': This is the second part of the commentary phrase; its purpose is to transmit an objection. Objection: This circularity defect applies only to the first jurist, because the first mujtahid himself derived these qiyasi issues. Now if knowing these issues is necessary for him, then circularity would occur because they are the result of his juristic ability. But if for later mujtahids knowing the qiyasi issues derived by the first mujtahid is necessary, then circularity does not arise, because these issues are the result of the first jurist's ability, not the second's. Since they are not the result of the second jurist's ability, they are not dependent on the second jurist's ability. Now juristic ability is dependent on qiyasi issues, but qiyasi issues are dependent on the first mujtahid's ability, not the second's, so circularity does not arise. Answer: 'Qulna': This is the third part of the commentary phrase; its purpose is to answer that question: circularity also applies to the second mujtahid, because imitation (taqlid) is not permissible for a mujtahid. Rather, the second jurist will himself perform ijtihad in these issues. When he knows them through ijtihad, his juristic ability is dependent on these qiyasi issues, and the qiyasi issues become dependent on his juristic ability because of his ijtihad. If this is not circularity, what is? 'Tam': This is the fourth part of the commentary phrase; its purpose is to state a benefit: for the second mujtahid (the statements of the first mujtahid)...
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of why qiyasi issues (analogical rulings) are excluded from the definition of fiqh to avoid circular reasoning (dawr). It begins by quoting the matn phrase 'la al-masa’il al-qiyasiyya' and explains Taftazani's purpose: including them would lead to dawr because a jurist's fiqaha depends on understanding these issues, and if they are part of fiqh, then fiqh depends on itself. The passage then presents an objection: this circularity only applies to the first mujtahid who derived the issues, not to later mujtahids who can rely on his derivation. The response (Qulna) rejects this: taqlid is not allowed for a mujtahid; the second mujtahid must independently derive these issues, causing circularity for him as well. The fourth part (Tam) begins to state a benefit but is cut off. The overall argument demonstrates that the definition of fiqh must exclude qiyasi issues to maintain logical coherence.

Key Terms
دور (dawr): Circular dependency where a thing's existence depends on itself, which is logically invalid.
مسائل قیاسیہ (masā’il qiyāsiyya): Rulings derived through analogy (qiyas); they are branches (furu‘) that depend on ijtihad.
تقليد (taqlīd): Following another mujtahid without independent evidence; not permissible for a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the later mujtahid also face circularity when qiyasi issues are included in fiqh?
A) Because he must consult the first mujtahid's works.
B) Because taqlid is forbidden for him, so he must derive qiyasi issues himself.
C) Because the definition of fiqh is fixed.
D) Because he lacks the ability to derive rulings.

Key Takeaway
Qiyasi issues are excluded from the definition of fiqh because including them leads to circularity (dawr), a logical defect that cannot be avoided even for later mujtahids due to the prohibition of taqlid for mujtahids.

Excluding Qiyasi Masail to Avoid Circularity in Defining Fiqh
Logical argument on definitional scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi argument against including qiyasi masail in the definition of fiqh and evaluate the counter-objection based on the prohibition of taqlid for mujtahids.

Core Idea
Including qiyasi masail in the definition of fiqh creates an invalid circular dependency (dawr).

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih explains why Taftazani excludes analogical rulings (qiyasi masail) from the definition of fiqh. The reason is to prevent circularity: if fiqh is defined as knowledge of all rulings, including those derived through ijtihad, then understanding fiqh would require understanding qiyasi masail, which themselves require the very juristic ability (fiqahat) that defines fiqh. The passage then addresses an objection and provides a decisive answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitional issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the definition of fiqh: whether it includes qiyasi masail or not.
The definition is about the scope of fiqh as a discipline.
2
Understand the circular dependency
Trace the dependency: fiqh depends on qiyasi masail (as parts of its subject matter). Qiyasi masail depend on ijtihad, which is the exercise of fiqh. Thus fiqh depends on itself.
This is the logical problem of dawr.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection claims that circularity only applies to the first mujtahid; later jurists can learn qiyasi masail without deriving them.
The objection assumes later jurists can rely on transmitted knowledge.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response asserts that later mujtahids cannot do taqlid; they must exercise ijtihad themselves, so the dependency remains.
Thus circularity applies universally to all mujtahids.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مسائل قیاسیہ کا علم فقہ کی تعریف میں شرط نہیں

جواب: قلنا یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض اسی سوال کا جواب ہے کہ دوسرے مجتہد کے لئے بھی دور لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ مجتہد کے لئے تقلید جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ فقیہ ثانی ان مسائل میں بھی خود اجتہاد کرے گا جب اجتہاد کے ذریعے جانے گا تو اس کی فقاہت ان مسائل قیاسیہ پر موقوف ہوگی اور مسائل قیاسیہ اسکے اجتہاد کی وجہ سے فقاہت پر موقوف ہو نگے یہ دور نہیں تو اور کیا ہے۔
Explanation: The knowledge of analogical matters is not a condition in the definition of fiqh. His saying 'not the analogical matters': This is the first part of the passage, in which the purpose is that Taftazani clarifies the text of al-Tawdih: that knowing the analogical matters is not necessary for fiqh, because in such a case circularity (dawr) would occur. That is such that understanding analogical matters depends on the jurist's jurisprudence (fiqahat), because analogical matters are the name for branches derived through ijtihad. So as long as the jurist does not have the capacity for jurisprudence and ijtihad, the derivation of these matters will not occur. Now if analogical matters are included in the definition of fiqh, then understanding fiqh will depend on understanding analogical matters, because the existence of the whole depends on its parts. Thus juristic reasoning itself would depend on itself through the intermediary of analogical matters, because a thing's dependence on what it depends on results in dependence on itself. This is the dependence of a thing on itself, which is circularity, and circularity is invalid, so that which necessitates circularity is also invalid. If it is said: This is the second part of the commentary, in which the objection is transmitted. Objection: The circularity defect applies to the first jurist, because the first mujtahid himself derived these analogical matters. Now if knowing these matters is necessary for him, then circularity would occur because they are the result of his jurisprudence. But if for later mujtahids knowing the analogical matters derived by the previous mujtahid is necessary, then circularity does not arise because these matters are the result of the first jurist's jurisprudence, not the second's. Since they are not the result of the second jurist's jurisprudence, they do not depend on the second's jurisprudence. Now jurisprudence would depend on analogical matters, but analogical matters would depend on the first mujtahid's jurisprudence, not the second's, so circularity does not occur. Answer: We say: This is the third part of the commentary, in which the answer to this question is that circularity also applies to the second mujtahid, because taqlid is not permissible for a mujtahid. Rather, the second jurist will also exercise ijtihad in these matters. When he learns through ijtihad, his jurisprudence will depend on these analogical matters, and the analogical matters, due to his ijtihad, will depend on jurisprudence. If this is not circularity, what is?
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a dispute from the commentary on al-Tawdih. The commentator explains Taftazani's clarification that the definition of fiqh should exclude qiyasi masail (analogical matters) to avoid circularity. The logic: If fiqh is defined as knowledge of all rulings including derived ones, then understanding fiqh would require understanding qiyasi masail, which themselves require juristic ability (fiqahat) and ijtihad. This creates a dependency loop, which is invalid. An objection is raised that this only applies to the first mujtahid; later mujtahids can learn from earlier ones without circularity. The response is that later mujtahids cannot do taqlid; they must derive rulings themselves, so the circularity remains for them as well. This is a classic Hanafi usul argument about the definition of fiqh and the nature of ijtihad.

Key Terms
مسائل قیاسیہ (masa'il qiyasiyya): Fiqh rulings derived through qiyas (analogical reasoning) as opposed to those directly from revelation.
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning or dependency where A depends on B and B depends on A; considered invalid in usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the circularity argument apply to later mujtahids?
A) They rely on earlier mujtahids.
B) They must derive rulings themselves.
C) They do not know qiyasi masail.
D) They are not mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh excludes qiyasi masail to avoid the logical fallacy of circularity (dawr), a fundamental principle in Usul al-Fiqh.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Status of Qiyasi Masail: Are They from Revelation?
Objection and two answers on whether qiyasi masail belong to fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul excludes qiyasi masail from the definition of fiqh and state the two answers given in the text.

Core Idea
Qiyas manifests rulings only relative to the mujtahid; directness without intermediary is required for 'from revelation'.

This passage presents a strong objection: if qiyas merely manifests rulings that are in principle derived from revelation, then qiyasi masail should count as fiqh. The Hanafi response has two layers: first, that manifestation is relative and can be erroneous; second, that the definition requires directness (bila wasita), which qiyas lacks due to the mujtahid's mental intermediary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the objection carefully: because qiyas is a 'muzhir' (manifestor) not 'muthbit' (establisher), the rulings it produces are still from revelation. Therefore, the second mujtahid must know the first mujtahid's qiyasi masail.
The opponent assumes that manifesting is equivalent to directly conveying revelation.
2
First Answer: Relative Manifestation
The manifestation occurred for the earlier mujtahid subjectively; in actuality (fī nafs al-amr) it may not be from revelation because ijtihad can err. Hence, the second mujtahid is not bound by them.
This answer highlights that qiyasi masail are not certain ('qat'i'), they are zanni.
3
Second Answer: Directness Required
The phrase 'whose manifestation occurred from revelation' means directly without intermediary. Qiyasi masail involve the mujtahid's mind as an intermediary, so they are excluded from the definition.
This clarifies the definition's condition: 'bila wasita'.
4
Apply the Conclusion
For a later mujtahid, knowledge of earlier qiyasi masail is not necessary; he must follow his own ijtihad. Taqlid is not permissible for him in these matters.
This underscores the independence required of a mujtahid.

Source Text

فان قیل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اس میں غرض ایک سوال کو ذکر کئے اس کے دو جواب دینا ہے۔ کوذکر دوجو سوال :۔ آپ مسائل قیاسیہ کو فقہ کی تعریف سے نکالنے کا دعویٰ کر رہے ہیں حالانکہ آپ کی تعریف میں مسائل قیاسیہ داخل ہیں وہ ایسے کہ فقہ نام ہے ان تمام احکام کے جاننے کا جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہوا ہو اور ان مسائل قیاسیہ کا نزول وحی سے ہو چکا کیونکہ قیاس مظہر احکام ہے نہ کہ مثبت احکام جب مسائل قیاسیہ کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو چکا ہے تو فقہ سے کیسے خارج کر رہے ہیں لہذا اب مجتہد ثانی کے لئے مجتہد اول کے مسائل قیاسیہ کا جاننا ضروری ہونا چاہیے۔ جواب (۱):۔ کہ ان مسائل قیاسیہ میں جو نزول وحی کا ظہور ہوا ہے وہ مجتہد سابق کے لئے ہوا ہے واقع اور نفس الامر میں نزول وحی کا ظہور نہیں ہوا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ مجتہد نے ان مسائل قیاسیہ میں غلطی کی ہولان المجتهد يخطى ويصيب _ای طرح مجتہد ثانی کے لئے بھی ان مسائل قیاسیہ کا ظہور نزول وحی سے نہیں ہوا ہے کیونکہ اس کے لئے لازم ہے کہ یہ اپنے اجتہاد پر عمل کرے اس کیلئے تقلید جائز نہیں ہے لہذا مجتہد لاحق کے لئے ان مسائل قیاسیہ کی معرفت ضروری نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۲): یمکن سے متن میں کہا کہ جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہوا ہو اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ بلا واسطہ ظہور ہوا ہو جبکہ مسائل قیاسیہ میں مجتہد کے ذہن کے واسطہ سے نزول وحی کا ظہور ہوتا ہے فلہذا یہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں اس لئے مجید ثانی کے لئے ان کا جاننا شرط بھی نہیں ہے۔
ثم طبنا ابحاث:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے اس میں شارع نے ماتن کی تعریف پر چند اعتراضات کئے ہیں ۔ الاول:۔ پہلا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے جو تعریف کی ہے یہ فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ فقہ مخصوص مسائل اور مخصوص علم کا نام ہے جیسے دوسرے علوم متعین مسائل کا نام ہیں حالانکہ ماتن کی تعریف سے سمجھ میں آتا ہے کہ فقہ ایک مفہوم کلی کا نام ہے جو زمانے کے تبدیل ہونے سے تبدیل ہوتا رہتا ہے مثلاً کم زیادہ ہوتا رہتا ہے جیسے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں وحی کے اور
If it is said: This is the fifth part of the commentary, in which the purpose is to mention a question and give two answers. The question: You claim to exclude analogical matters from the definition of fiqh, whereas your definition includes them. Such that fiqh is the name for knowing all rulings whose manifestation occurred from revelation, and these analogical matters have manifested from revelation because qiyas manifests rulings, not establishes them. Since the manifestation of analogical matters from revelation has occurred, how can you exclude them from fiqh? Therefore, for the second mujtahid, knowing the first mujtahid's analogical matters should be necessary. Answer (1): The manifestation of revelation in these analogical matters occurred for the previous mujtahid; in reality and in actual fact, the manifestation of revelation did not occur, because it is possible that the mujtahid erred in these analogical matters, while the mujtahid may err and may be correct. Similarly, for the second mujtahid, the manifestation of these analogical matters from revelation has not occurred, because it is necessary for him to act upon his own ijtihad; taqlid is not permissible for him. Therefore, for the later mujtahid, knowledge of these analogical matters is not necessary. Answer (2): It is possible, from the text, that what is meant by 'whose manifestation from revelation occurred' is that the manifestation occurred without an intermediary, whereas in analogical matters, the manifestation of revelation occurs through the intermediary of the mujtahid's mind. Hence, these analogical matters are not included in fiqh. Therefore, for the second mujtahid, knowing them is not a condition. Then we turn to discussions: This is the last part of the commentary, in which the commentator has made several objections to the definition of the matn. The first: The definition given by the matn contradicts the technical definition of fiqh, because fiqh is the name for specific issues and specific knowledge, like other sciences are names for specific sets of issues. However, the matn's definition implies that fiqh is the name for a general concept that changes with the change of time, e.g., it increases and decreases, like in the time of the Messenger (peace be upon him) revelation...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage contains a further objection and two answers, followed by Taftazani's criticisms. The objection argues that qiyasi masail are from revelation because qiyas merely manifests rulings from the revealed sources, so they should be included. The first answer distinguishes between actual revelation and revelation as it appears to a particular mujtahid; since mujtahids can err, qiyasi masail are not necessarily from revelation in reality. The second answer clarifies that the definition's phrase 'from revelation' means directly without intermediary; qiyasi masail involve the mujtahid's mind as an intermediary, so they are excluded. Then Taftazani raises objections, the first being that the definition makes fiqh a changing concept, while it should be a fixed body of knowledge like other sciences. This is a critical refinement of the matn's definition.

Key Terms
مظہر (muzhir): That which manifests or reveals something; qiyas is described as mazhir al-ahkam (manifestor of rulings) not muthbit (establisher).
بالا واسطہ (bila wasita): Without intermediary; directly from revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second answer given to the objection that qiyasi masail are from revelation?
A) Qiyas is not a valid source of law.
B) The definition requires direct manifestation without intermediary; qiyas involves the mujtahid's mind as an intermediary.
C) The second mujtahid must follow the first mujtahid's qiyasi masail.
D) Qiyasi masail are not from revelation because they are based on custom.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis exclude qiyasi masail from the definition of fiqh because they are not directly from revelation; they involve the intermediary of ijtihad and are subject to error.

Taftazani's First Objection: Fiqh as a Changing Concept
Taftazani's first criticism of the matn's definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Taftazani's first criticism of the matn's definition and explain why it challenges the definition as stating a constant body of knowledge.

Core Idea
Taftazani objects that the definition makes fiqh a historically relative concept, not a fixed science.

After defending the exclusion of qiyasi masail, the commentator turns to Taftazani's criticisms of the matn's definition itself. The first criticism is that the definition implies fiqh is not a fixed set of issues but a concept that expands and contracts over time, contradicting the nature of a defined science.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Criticism
Taftazani argues that according to the matn's definition, fiqh would be a general meaning that changes over time (e.g., increasing with new revelations). But fiqh, like other sciences, should be defined by specific, unchanging issues.
The criticism targets the wording 'knowing all rulings whose manifestation occurred from revelation' — this seems to make fiqh dependent on historical revelation.
2
Identify the Key Concept
The issue is whether fiqh is a 'mafhum kulli' (universal concept) that applies to changing instances, or a 'science' with fixed subject matter.
Taftazani leans toward the latter; the matn's definition may be insufficient.
3
Relate to the Overall Debate
This objection challenges the core definition given earlier. The commentator will likely respond later, but the passage cuts off.
Consider how this relates to the earlier objection about qiyasi masail.

Distinguishing Haqiqi and Mudawwan Fiqh in Hanafi Usul
Objection and response on qiyasi issues and fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi fiqh and mudawwan fiqh, and apply this distinction to classify whether a qiyasi issue belongs to the essential definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
Qiyasi issues are not part of haqiqi fiqh but are included in mudawwan fiqh for practical benefit.

This lesson addresses a critical objection to the definition of fiqh: that it excludes qiyasi issues, which form a major part of fiqh works. The Hanafi response resolves this by distinguishing between the essential core of fiqh (based on revelation and consensus) and the compiled body of fiqh that includes analogically derived rulings for practical use. Understanding this distinction clarifies the epistemological status of qiyas in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Understand the claim that the matn's definition of fiqh excludes qiyasi issues, even though they constitute the majority of fiqh topics.
The objection is that if fiqh is only nass and ijma', then qiyasi issues are not fiqh.
2
Examine the initial response
The text first suggests that qiyasi issues are fiqh for the mujtahid who derives them, because for him they are linked to revelation.
This answer is partial and leads to a new problem.
3
Recognize the problem
If each mujtahid's qiyasi rulings are considered fiqh only for him, then fiqh becomes relative to each mujtahid, contradicting the unity of fiqh.
The passage asks: should fiqh be one or many?
4
Apply the key distinction
The resolution distinguishes haqiqi fiqh (real fiqh: rulings from nass or ijma') from mudawwan fiqh (compiled fiqh: includes qiyasi issues for convenience).
Haqiqi fiqh is universal; mudawwan fiqh can vary.
5
Derive the resolution
Qiyasi issues are outside haqiqi fiqh but are included in mudawwan fiqh. Diversity in mudawwan fiqh is acceptable and does not harm the essential unity of fiqh.
This preserves the classical definition while accommodating common usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث:۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ مصنف کی تعریف سے مسائل قیاسیہ نکل گئے حالانکہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ کے معظم مسائل میں سے شمار ہوتے ہیں تو ماتن کی تعریف سے فقہ کا معتد بہ حصہ خارج ہوگا۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ کا جس مجتہد نے استنباط کیا ہے اس کے حق میں فقہ میں داخل ہیں کیونکہ اس کے نزدیک ان مسائل کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو چکا ہے دوسرے مجتہد کے حق میں نزول وحی سے ظہور نہیں ہوا جس نے اجتہاد کیا اس کے حق میں مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ کی تعریف میں داخل ہونگے لیکن اس جواب کی صورت میں ایک خرابی لازم آئے گی کہ ہر مجتہد کی فقہ الگ ہو اس صورت میں امام صاحب نے جن مسائل کا استنباط کیا وہ ان کے نزدیک فقہ ہے ایسے ہی امام مالک نے جن مسائل کا استنباط کیا وہ ان کے نزدیک فقہ ہے وغیر ذلک تو ہر امام کی فقہ مختلف ہو گئی حالانکہ فقہ ایک ہونی چاہئیے خلاصہ یہ کہ ہر مجتہد کی فقہ پر یہ تعریف صادق نہیں آئے گی۔ جواب: - حقیقہ فقہ دو چیزوں کا نام ہے وہ احکام منصوصہ وحی سے جن کا ظہور ہوا ہواوروہ احکام کہ ان پر اجتماع کا انعقاد ہوا ہو یہ تعریف تمام مجتہدین کی فقہ پر صادق آتی ہے باقی مسائل قیاسیہ یہ حقیقتہ فقہ سے خارج ہیں یہ عوام کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے فقہ میں داخل اور ذکر کئے گئے ہیں (خلاصہ) یہ کہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ حقیقی میں داخل نہیں البتہ فقہ مدون میں داخل ہیں اور اگر فقہ مدون مختلف ہو جائے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔
The third objection: The author's definition excludes qiyasi (analogical) issues, although qiyasi issues are counted among the most important issues of fiqh. So a significant part of fiqh would be excluded by the matn's definition. Answer: Qiyasi issues are included in fiqh for the mujtahid who derived them, because in his view, these issues have become apparent through revelation. For another mujtahid, they have not become apparent through revelation. So for the one who performed ijtihad, qiyasi issues are included in the definition of fiqh. But this answer entails a problem: each mujtahid's fiqh would be separate. In that case, the issues that Imam Abu Hanifa derived are fiqh according to him, similarly Imam Malik's derived issues are fiqh according to him, etc. So each imam's fiqh would be different, whereas fiqh should be one. Summary: This definition would not apply to every mujtahid's fiqh. Answer: The reality of fiqh is the name of two things: those injunctions that have become apparent through revelation (nass) and those injunctions on which consensus (ijma') has occurred. This definition applies to all mujtahids' fiqh. As for qiyasi issues, they are outside the reality of fiqh. They are included and mentioned in fiqh out of consideration for the common people. Summary: Qiyasi issues are not included in haqiqi (real) fiqh, but they are included in mudawwan (compiled/organized) fiqh. And if mudawwan fiqh differs, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage addresses the third objection: the definition of fiqh excludes issues derived through qiyas (analogy), even though these form a major part of fiqh. The initial response suggests that qiyasi issues are fiqh for the mujtahid who derives them, but this leads to a problem: each mujtahid's fiqh would be different. The final response resolves this by distinguishing between haqiqi (real) fiqh, which consists only of revealed commands (nass) and ijma', and mudawwan (compiled) fiqh, which includes qiyasi issues for practical benefit. Thus, qiyasi issues are not part of the essential reality of fiqh but are included for the sake of the community. This distinction preserves the unity of fiqh in its essence while allowing diversity in its compiled form.

Key Terms
فقہ حقیقی (fiqh haqiqi): Real fiqh: rulings based directly on revelation (Qur'an and Sunnah) or consensus (ijma').
فقہ مدون (fiqh mudawwan): Compiled/organized fiqh: includes qiyasi issues for practical use, even if not part of haqiqi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of qiyasi issues in relation to haqiqi fiqh?
A) They are an integral part of haqiqi fiqh.
B) They are excluded from both haqiqi and mudawwan fiqh.
C) They are not part of haqiqi fiqh but are included in mudawwan fiqh.
D) They are haqiqi fiqh for the mujtahid who derives them only.

Key Takeaway
Qiyasi issues are not part of haqiqi fiqh (nass/ijma') but are legitimately included in mudawwan fiqh for practical benefit, preserving the essence of fiqh while accommodating diversity.

Qiyas and Certainty in Fiqh
Refining the definition of fiqh by excluding zanni rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the epistemological status of qiyas-derived rulings as zanni and explain why they are outside haqiqi fiqh.

Core Idea
Rulings from qiyas are zanni, not qat'i, so outside haqiqi fiqh.

This passage refines the definition of fiqh by clarifying that only certain (qat'i) rulings belong to its essential core. Qiyas, being speculative, produces zanni rulings that are excluded from haqiqi fiqh, even though they are recorded in fiqh books for practical use. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi epistemological hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The passage asserts that what qiyas shows as revelation is outside fiqh. Look for the phrase 'خَارِجٌ عَن الْفِقْهِ'.
The claim directly excludes qiyas from the essential reality of fiqh.
2
Determine the basis
The basis is that it is certain (qat'i) that qiyas yields zanni (speculative) knowledge. The passage uses 'لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّهُ ظَنّى'—meaning we are certain that qiyas is speculative.
Zanni here refers to the epistemological status of the derived ruling.
3
Compare with nass and ijma'
The passage notes that even nass (text) and ijma' are qat'i only if their transmission (thubut) is also qat'i. This highlights the importance of thubut in determining certainty.
Thubut refers to the chain of transmission; ahad reports are zanni in thubut.
4
Recognize the implication for ahad reports
Rulings from ahad reports are also zanni, as stated explicitly: 'الْأَحْكامَ الثَّابِتَةَ بِأَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ ظَنِّيَّةٌ'. Thus, they too are not part of haqiqi fiqh.
This extends the exclusion to all rulings based on zanni adillah.
5
Synthesize the core distinction
Only rulings with both qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala constitute haqiqi fiqh. Qiyas and ahad reports produce practical rulings but are epistemologically inferior.
Haqiqi fiqh refers to the essential, certain core of juristic knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ) فَجَوَابُهُ أَوَّلًا ) مُشْعِرٌ بِأَنَّ مَا أَظْهَرَ الْقِيَاسُ نُزُولَ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ فَهُوَ خَارِجٌ عَنْ الْفِقْهِ لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّهُ ظَنّى ، ثُمَّ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ النَّصُّ أَوْ الْإِجْمَاعُ أَيْضًا إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ قَطْعِيًّا إذَا كَانَ ثُبُوتُهُمَا أَيْضًا قَطْعِيًّا لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّ الْأَحْكامَ الثَّابِتَةَ بِأَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ ظَنِّيَّةٌ
His statement: 'So his answer first' indicates that what qiyas shows as revelation is outside fiqh because it is certain that it is zanni (speculative). Then, what is established by nass (text) or ijma' is also qat'i (certain) only if their thubut (proof) is also qat'i, because it is certain that rulings established by ahad reports are zanni.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This short Arabic passage from the commentary reinforces the third objection's resolution. It states that rulings derived through qiyas (analogy) are outside the essential reality of fiqh because they are zanni (speculative) by nature. Even rulings from nass (Qur'an or mutawatir hadith) and ijma' are only qat'i (certain) if their transmission (thubut) is also qat'i. Rulings from ahad reports are zanni, and thus also not part of the certain core. This underscores the idea that haqiqi fiqh consists only of definitively proven rulings, while qiyas and ahad-based rulings are included in fiqh mudawwan for practical application.

Key Terms
ظنی (zanni): Speculative or probable; not certain. Used for rulings that are not definitively proven.
قطعی (qat'i): Certain and definitive; rulings established by mutawatir or ijma' with qat'i thubut.
ثبوت (thubut): Proof or transmission; the chain of narration or evidence establishing the source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of rulings derived from qiyas?
A) They are qat'i and part of haqiqi fiqh.
B) They are zanni and outside haqiqi fiqh.
C) They are zanni but still considered haqiqi fiqh.
D) They are qat'i only if based on ahad hadith.

Key Takeaway
Only rulings with qat'i thubut and dalala constitute haqiqi fiqh; qiyas produces zanni rulings and is thus excluded.

The Certainty of Fiqh: The Objection from Qiyasi Issues
Response to first objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between fiqh haqiqi and fiqh mudawwan to defend the definitive nature of fiqh against the objection from qiyasi issues.

Core Idea
Qiyasi issues are in compiled fiqh, not real fiqh; fiqh remains qat'i.

This lesson examines the first objection against fiqh being definitive knowledge: if fiqh is only rulings from revelation and ijma, then qiyasi issues would be excluded. The response introduces a crucial distinction between real fiqh (fiqh haqiqi) and compiled fiqh (fiqh mudawwan). Understanding this distinction is essential for appreciating how the Hanafi school maintains the certainty of fiqh despite the use of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection claims that if fiqh is defined only as rulings from nas and ijma, then qiyasi issues would be excluded from fiqh, yet they constitute the majority of fiqh issues.
The commentator raises this as an objection to the matn's earlier answer.
2
Understand the distinction
The response distinguishes fiqh haqiqi (real fiqh) – the rulings themselves from nas and ijma – from fiqh mudawwan (compiled fiqh) – the collected rulings including qiyasi issues.
Qiyasi issues are part of the compiled work, but their certainty derives from the definitive basis of the original rulings.
3
Apply the distinction
Since qiyasi issues are included in fiqh mudawwan but not in fiqh haqiqi, the objection that they would be excluded from fiqh is answered: they are included in the broader compiled sense.
The text states the answer has already passed, meaning the distinction was made earlier in the commentary.
4
Conclude
The objection fails because it conflates two senses of fiqh. The definitive nature of fiqh remains intact as its core (nas and ijma) is qat'i.
This sets the stage for further objections about thubut and zann.

Source Text

تشریح: قولہ فجوابہ اولا:۔ اس عبارت میں شارع نے دو اعتراض کئے ہیں ماقبل میں ماتن نے اعتراض کا جواب دیا تھا اعتراض یہ تھا ماتن پر کہ فقہ ظنی ہے اور خلیات پر علم کا اطلاق نہیں ہوتا تو فقہ کو علم الفقہ نہیں کہنا چاہیے تو ماتن نے جواب دیا تھا کہ فقہ نام ہے ان احکام کا جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہوا ہو یا ان پر اجماع منعقد ہوا ہو اور یہ قطعی ہیں تو علم الفقہ کہنا صحیح ہے اب شاریخ نے دو اعتراض کئے ہیں۔ اعتراض (۱)۔ اس سے لازم آئے گا کہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ سے خارج ہوں حالانکہ یہ فقہ کے معظم مسائل میں سے ہیں جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقہ مدون میں داخل ہیں نہ کہ فقہ حقیقی میں یہ جواب ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے لہذا اب اعتراض نہ رہا۔ اعتراض (۲) ۔ گویا کہ آپ نے کہا کہ جن احکام پر اجماع کا انعقاد ہوا ہو یا ان پر نزول وحی کا ظہور ہوا ہو یہ یقینا قطعی ہیں ہم ان کا قطعی ہونا تسلیم نہیں کرتے کیونکہ وہ قطعی تب ہو سکتے ہیں جب ان کا ثبوت بھی قطعی ہو اس لئے کہ اگر حکم خبر واحد سے ثابت ہو تو یہ ثبوت قطعی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کو ظنی کہتے ہیں ایسے ہی اجماع سے جو احکام ثابت ہوں یہ بھی قطعی ہوں یہ نہیں مانتے
