احْتِمَالِهِ الصَّدْقَ وَالْكَذِبَ خَبَرًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِفَادَتِهِ الْحُكْمَ إِخْبَارًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ جُزْءا مِنْ الدَّلِيلِ مُقَدَّمَةً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يُطْلَبُ بِالدَّلِيلِ مَطْلُوبًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ يَحُصُلُ مِنْ الدَّلِيلِ نَتِيجَةً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ يَقَعُ فِى الْعِلْمِ وَيُسْأَلُ عَنْهُ مَسْأَلَة فَالذَّاتُ وَاحِدَةٌ وَاخْتِلَافُ الْعِبَارَاتِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الاعْتِبَارَاتِ وَالْمَحْكُومُ عَلَيْهِ فِى الْقَضِيَّةِ يُسَمَّى مَوْضُوعًا وَالْمَحْكُومُ بِهِ مَحْمُولًا وَمَوْضُوعُ المَطْلُوبِ يُسَمَّى أَصْغَرَ وَمَحْمُولُهُ أَكْبَرَ وَالدِّلِيلُ يَتَأَلفُ لَا مَحَالَةَ مِنْ مُقَدِّمَتَيْنِ تَشْتَمِلُ إِحْدَيْهُمَا عَلَى الْأَصْغَرِ وَتُسَمَّى الصُّغُرَى وَالْأُخْرَى عَلَى الأَكْبَرِ وَتُسَمَّى الْكُبْرَى وَكِلْتَاهُمَا مُشْتَمِل عَلَى أَمْرٍ مُتَكَرِّرٍ فِيهِمَا يُسَمَّى الْأَوْسَطَ ، وَالْأَوْسَطُ إِمَّا مَحْمُولٌ فِى الصُّغُرَى مَوْضُوعٌ فِي الْكُبْرَى وَيُسَمَّى الدَّلِيلُ بِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ الشَّكْلَ الأَوَّلَ أَوْ بِالْعَكْسِ وَيُسَمَّى الشَّكْلَ الرَّابِعَ أَوْ مَحْمُولٌ فِيهِمَا وَيُسَمَّى الشَّكْلَ الثَّانِي أَوْ مَوْضُوعٌ فِيهِمَا وَيُسَمَّى الشَّكْلَ الثَّالِكِ مثلا إِذَا قُلْنَا الْحَجَّ وَاجِبٌ ؛ لأنَّهُ مَأْمُورُ الشَّارِعِ وَكُلُّ مَا هُوَ مَأْمُورُ الشَّارِعِ فَهُوَ وَاجِبٌ فَالْحَجُّ الْأَصْغَرُ وَالْوَاجِبُ الْأَكْبَرُ وَالْمَأْمُورُ الْأَوْسَطُ وَقَوْلُنَا الْحَج مَأْمُرُ: الشَّارِعِ هِيَ الصُّغُرَى وَقَوْلُنَا وَكُلُّ مَا هُوَ مَأْمُورُ الشَّارِعِ فَهُوَ وَاجِبٌ هِيَ الْكُبْرَى وَالدَّلِيلُ المَذْكُورُ مِنْ الشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ فَالْقَوَاعِدُ الَّتِي يُتَوَكَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ هِيَ الْقَضَايَا الْكُلّيّةُ الَّتِي تَقَعُ كُبُرَى لِصْغُرَى سَهْلَةِ الْحُصُولِ عِنْدَ الاسْتِدْلَالِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ كَمَا فِى الْمِثَالِ الْمَذْكُورِ وَضَمُّ الْقَاعِدَةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ إِلَى الصُّغُرَى السَّهْلَةِ الْحُصُولِ لِيَخْرُجَ المَطْلُوبُ الْفِقْهِيُّ مِنْ الْقُوَّةِ إِلَى الْفِعْلِ هُوَ مَعْنَى التَّوَصْلِ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ لَكِنْ تَحْصِيلَ الْقَاعِدَةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ يَتَوَفَّفُ عَلَى الْبَحْثِ عَنْ أَحْوَالِ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَبَيَانِ شَرَائِطِهِمَا وَقُيُودِهِمَا الْمُعْتَبَرَةِ فِي كُلِّيَّةِ الْقَاعِدَةِ فَالمَبَاحِثُ المُتَعَلَّقَهُ بِذَلِكَ هِيَ مَطَالِبُ أَصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَتَنْدَرِجُ كُلُّهَا تَحْتَ الْعِلْمِ بِالْقَاعِدَةِ عَلَى مَا شَرَحَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِمَا لَا مَزِيدَ عَلَيْهِ .
His statement: 'And by universal propositions I mean...' Know that a complete composite that is susceptible to truth and falsehood is called, from the perspective of its inclusion of a judgment, a 'qadiyya'; from the perspective of its susceptibility to truth and falsehood, 'khabar'; from the perspective of its conveying the judgment, 'ikhbar'; from the perspective of it being a part of a proof, 'muqaddima'; from the perspective that it is sought by proof, 'matlub'; from the perspective that it is obtained from proof, 'natija'; and from the perspective that it occurs in knowledge and is asked about, 'mas'ala'. The essence is one, and the difference in terminology is due to different considerations. The subject of the judgment in a qadiyya is called 'mawdu' and the predicate 'mahmul'. The subject of the matlub is called 'asghar' and its predicate 'akbar'. A proof necessarily consists of two premises, one containing the asghar and called 'sughra', the other containing the akbar and called 'kubra'. Both premises share a repeated term called 'awsat'. The awsat may be predicate in the sughra and subject in the kubra — the proof is then called 'first figure'; or the opposite — 'fourth figure'; or predicate in both — 'second figure'; or subject in both — 'third figure'. For example, when we say: 'Hajj is obligatory because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' So 'Hajj' is the asghar, 'obligatory' is the akbar, and 'commanded by the Lawgiver' is the awsat. Our statement 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' is the sughra, and our statement 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' is the kubra. The mentioned proof is of the first figure. Thus the rules (qawa'id) relied upon for fiqh are the universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that serve as the kubra for an easily obtainable sughra when deducing fiqh masail by the first figure, as in the example. Combining the universal rule with the easily obtainable sughra to bring the fiqh sought from potentiality to actuality is the meaning of 'tawassul biha ila al-fiqh'. But the acquisition of the universal rule depends on investigating the states of proofs and rulings and explaining their conditions and relevant restrictions for the universality of the rule. So the discussions pertaining to that are the topics of usul al-fiqh, and all of them fall under the knowledge of the rule, as the author explained in a manner beyond which there is no further.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a foundational definition from the Talwih commentary. It defines the concept of 'qadiyya' (proposition) from various angles (truth, judgment, part of proof, etc.) and then explains the structure of a syllogism (qiyas) as used in Hanafi usul. The example given is: Hajj is obligatory because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded is obligatory. This is a first-figure syllogism (shakl awwal) where the middle term (awsat) is 'commanded by the Lawgiver'. The text then identifies the 'qawa'id kulliyya' (universal rules) as major premises (kubra) in such syllogisms. The science of usul al-fiqh is precisely the investigation of these universal rules—how they are derived from the sources, their conditions, and their application. This passage is critical for understanding the logical underpinnings of Hanafi usul: fiqh rulings are derived by applying a universal rule (kubra) to a particular case (sughra) through syllogistic reasoning. The author emphasizes that the universal rules themselves are not innate but require deep research into the proofs and principles. This is a classic Hanafi approach blending logic (mantiq) with legal theory.

Key Terms
قضية (qadiyya): A complete composite statement containing a judgment, susceptible to truth/falsehood
مقدمة (muqaddima): A premise of a proof
صغرى (sughra): The minor premise containing the subject of the conclusion
كبرى (kubra): The major premise containing the predicate of the conclusion; also qa'ida kulliyya
أوسط (awsat): The middle term common to both premises
شكل أول (shakl awwal): First figure syllogism
قاعدة كلية (qa'ida kulliyya): A universal proposition used as major premise in fiqh deduction
مطلوب (matlub): The sought conclusion of a proof
نتيجة (natija): The conclusion obtained from proof
مسألة (mas'ala): A question that occurs in knowledge

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, what is the role of a 'qa'ida kulliyya' (universal rule) in deriving a fiqh ruling?
A) It is the minor premise of a syllogism
B) It is the major premise of a syllogism
C) It is the conclusion of a syllogism
D) It is the middle term of a syllogism

Key Takeaway
A qa'ida kulliyya is the major premise (kubra) in a first-figure syllogism that, combined with a specific minor premise (sughra), yields a fiqh ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Logical Terms and Syllogism in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining logical terms and the syllogistic method for fiqh reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven names of a proposition based on perspective and explain the structure of the first figure syllogism as used in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A syllogism combines a universal rule and a specific case to derive a fiqh ruling.

This passage introduces the logical framework underlying qiyas in Hanafi usul. Understanding these terms is essential for analyzing how rulings are derived from principles. The author systematically defines a proposition, its parts, and the syllogism figures with a fiqh example.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the seven names of a proposition
The same compound statement is called qadiyya (proposition), khabar (report), ikhbar (assertion), muqaddima (premise), matlub (desired), natija (conclusion), or mas'ala (issue) depending on the perspective (e.g., implication of ruling, truth-aptness, part of proof).
The essence is one; names differ by viewpoint.
2
Identify the components of a syllogism
A syllogism has two premises: the minor premise (sughra) contains the minor term (asghar), the major premise (kubra) contains the major term (akbar), and both share a middle term (hadd awsat).
The middle term appears in both premises but not in the conclusion.
3
Distinguish the four figures by position of the middle term
First figure: middle term is predicate in minor, subject in major. Second: predicate in both. Third: subject in both. Fourth: subject in minor, predicate in major.
The first figure is the most demonstrative and commonly used in fiqh.
4
Apply the first figure to the Hajj example
The syllogism 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver; everything commanded is obligatory; therefore Hajj is obligatory' uses the first figure. Hajj is the minor term, obligatory is the major, and 'commanded' is the middle.
The minor premise is the specific case; the major premise is the universal rule.
5
Understand the role of universal rules as major premises
The universal rules (qawa'id kulliyya) of fiqh serve as major premises in syllogisms. They are obtained by investigating the states of evidences and rulings—this is the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.
Combining the universal rule with an easily obtainable minor premise brings the fiqh conclusion from potentiality to actuality.

توصل ہوتا ہے ان كے ذریعہ فقہ تك وہ قضایا كلیہ ہیں جو صغری سھلتہ الحصول كیلئے كبری واقع ہوتے ہیں مسائل فقہ پر شكل اول كے ذریعہ استدلال كے وقت۔ جیسا كہ مثال مذكور میں ہے اور قاعدہ كلیہ كو ملا نا صغری پر اور ان كی شرائط كے بیان كرنے پر اور دونوں كی قیود پر جو معتبر ہیں قاعدہ كے كلیہ ہونے ميں ۔ پس وہ مباحث جو ان چیزوں كے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ اصول فقہ كے مطالب ہیں اور مندرج ہیں یہ تمام ( ابحاث ) قاعدہ كلیہ كے علم كے تحت۔ اس تفصیل پر كہ جو وضاحت كی ہے مصنف نے كہ اس پر زیادتی كی گنجائش نہیں ہے۔
اصطلاحات منطقیہ كا بیان
تشریح قول یعنی "بالقضایا":۔ یہ شرح كی عبارت كا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارع امتن میں مذكور لفظ قضیہ كا معنی بیان كرتا ہے اور اس مناسبت سے كچھ اصطلاحات كو بیان كرتا ہے۔
اصطلاح (۱): مركب كے سات نام ہیں (۱) قضیه (۲) خبر (۳) اخبار (۴) مقدمه (۵) مطلوب (۷) نتیجه (۷) مسئلہ۔ اس اصطلاح كا حاصل یہ ہے كه مركب نام جسے كلام كہا جاتا ہے مختلف حیثیات سے اس كے مختلف نام ہیں اور حقیقت
A syllogism necessarily consists of two premises, one of which contains the minor term and is called the minor premise, and the other contains the major term and is called the major premise, and both contain a repeated term called the middle term. The middle term is either predicated in the minor and subject in the major, called the first figure, or the opposite, called the fourth figure, or predicated in both, called the second figure, or subject in both, called the third figure. For example, when we say: 'Hajj is obligatory because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' So Hajj is the minor term, obligatory is the major term, and what is commanded is the middle term. Our statement 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' is the minor premise, and our statement 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' is the major premise, and the mentioned syllogism belongs to the first figure. The rules by which one reaches fiqh are the universal propositions that serve as major premises for easily obtainable minor premises when deducing fiqh issues via the first figure, as in the example. Attaching the universal rule to the easily obtainable minor premise to bring the fiqh conclusion from potentiality to actuality is the meaning of reaching fiqh through these rules. However, obtaining the universal rule depends on investigating the states of the evidences and rulings and explaining their conditions and relevant restrictions for the rule's universality. Thus, the discussions related to that are the topics of usul al-fiqh, and all of them fall under the knowledge of the rule, as the author explained with nothing more. Translation: Know that a complete compound that can be true or false is called 'qadiyya' (proposition) from the perspective of implying a ruling, 'khabar' from the perspective of being truth-apt, 'ikhbar' from the perspective of conveying a ruling, 'muqaddima' (premise) from being part of an argument, 'matlub' (desired) from being sought via the argument, 'natija' (conclusion) from being produced by the argument, and 'mas'ala' (issue) from occurring in knowledge and being questioned about. So the essence is one, and the titles differ due to different perspectives. In a proposition, the subject of the ruling is called 'mawdu'' (subject) and the predicate is called 'mahmul' (predicate). The subject of the sought conclusion is called 'asghar' (minor) and its predicate is called 'akbar' (major). A syllogism necessarily consists of two premises: one contains the minor and is called 'sughra' (minor premise), the other contains the major and is called 'kubra' (major premise), and both contain a repeated term called 'hadd awsat' (middle term). This middle term is either predicated in the minor and subject in the major, so the syllogism is called 'shakl awwal' (first figure), or the opposite, called 'shakl rabi''' (fourth figure), or predicated in both, called 'shakl thani' (second figure), or subject in both, called 'shakl thalith' (third figure). For example, when we say 'Hajj is obligatory because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory', then Hajj is the minor, obligatory is the major, and commanded is the middle term. Our statement 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' is the minor premise, and our statement 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' is the major premise. The mentioned syllogism is of the first figure. So the rules by which one reaches fiqh are the universal propositions that serve as major premises for easily obtainable minor premises when deducing fiqh issues via the first figure, as in the example. Attaching the universal rule to the easily obtainable minor premise to bring the fiqh conclusion from potentiality to actuality is the meaning of reaching fiqh through these rules. However, obtaining the universal rule depends on investigating the states of the evidences and rulings and explaining their conditions and relevant restrictions for the rule's universality. Thus, the discussions related to that are the topics of usul al-fiqh, and all of them fall under the knowledge of the rule, as the author explained concisely. Explanation: Elucidation of the statement 'by propositions': This is the first part of the commentary; the commentator intends to explain the meaning of the term 'qadiyya' mentioned in the text and accordingly explains some terms. Term (1): The compound has seven names: (1) qadiyya, (2) khabar, (3) ikhbar, (4) muqaddima, (5) matlub, (6) natija, (7) mas'ala. The gist of this term is that the compound called speech has different names from different perspectives, while its reality is one.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of logical terms and the structure of syllogism (qiyas) as applied to usul al-fiqh. The author begins by describing the syllogistic figure: the minor premise (sughra) contains the minor term (asghar), the major premise (kubra) contains the major term (akbar), and both share the middle term (awsaṭ). The arrangement of terms determines the figure: first figure (middle term predicated in minor, subject in major), second figure (predicated in both), third figure (subject in both), fourth figure (reverse of first). An example from fiqh is given: 'Hajj is obligatory because it is commanded by the Lawgiver; everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' Here, 'Hajj' is the minor term, 'obligatory' is the major term, and 'commanded by the Lawgiver' is the middle term. The minor premise is the specific case, and the major premise is the universal rule. The first figure is used to derive the fiqh ruling. The passage then explains that the universal rules (qawāʿid kulliyya) of fiqh serve as major premises, and when combined with easily obtained minor premises (specific cases), they produce the fiqh conclusion. The science of usul al-fiqh studies these universal rules by examining the sources (adilla), rulings (aḥkām), their conditions, and restrictions. The Urdu section elaborates that a complete compound that can be true or false is called qadiyya (proposition) when considered as implying a ruling, khabar when considered as truth-apt, ikhbar when conveying a ruling, muqaddima when part of a syllogism, matlub when sought via a proof, natija when derived from a proof, and mas'ala when it occurs in knowledge as a question. Thus, the same entity receives different names based on perspective. In a proposition, the subject is mawḍūʿ and the predicate is maḥmūl. In a syllogism, the subject of the conclusion is aṣghar, its predicate akbar, the premise containing the minor is ṣughrā, and the premise containing the major is kubrā. The repeated term is called ḥadd awsaṭ. The figures are then defined with the example of Hajj. Finally, the passage notes that the rules (qawāʿid) by which one reaches fiqh are universal propositions serving as major premises for easily obtained minor premises, and their discovery requires investigating the states of evidences and rulings—this is the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. All these discussions fall under the knowledge of the universal rule, as the author has explained sufficiently.

Key Terms
قضیہ (qadiyya): A complete compound that implies a ruling and is truth-apt; called by different names depending on perspective (e.g., khabar, muqaddima, matlub, natija, mas'ala).
حد اوسط (hadd awsaṭ): The middle term in a syllogism that appears in both premises but not in the conclusion; it connects the minor and major terms.
شکل اول (shakl awwal): The first figure of a syllogism where the middle term is predicated in the minor premise and subject in the major premise; considered the most natural and demonstrative form.
مقدمہ (muqaddima): A proposition considered as part of a syllogism, either as a premise.
صغری (sughra): The minor premise, containing the minor term (asghar) of the conclusion.
كبری (kubra): The major premise, containing the major term (akbar) of the conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which term is used for a proposition when it is considered as part of a proof (dalil)?
A) Qadiyya
B) Khabar
C) Muqaddima
D) Natija

Key Takeaway
A proposition has seven names depending on perspective; the first figure syllogism (middle term predicated in minor, subject in major) is the primary form for deriving fiqh rulings from universal principles.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Many Names of a Proposition: Qadiyya, Khabar, Ikbbar, Muqaddama, Matlub, Natija
Defining logical terms for a proposition from multiple perspectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical term for a proposition based on the perspective from which it is viewed.

Core Idea
A single proposition is named differently depending on its role: report, premise, demand, conclusion, or issue.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding logical terminology is essential for constructing sound analogies (qiyas). This lesson clarifies how the same proposition can be called by different names—khabar, ikhbar, muqaddama, matlub, natija, mas'ala—depending on the context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base proposition (qadiyya)
Locate a statement that carries a judgment, e.g., 'Zaid is standing'.
The proposition must have a subject and predicate.
2
Determine the perspective
Ask: Is it viewed as possibly true/false? Then it's khabar. Is it part of a proof? Then muqaddama. Is it being sought? Then matlub. Is it derived from proof? Then natija. Is it a questioned topic? Then mas'ala.
The perspective is a relation to other elements.
3
Apply the corresponding term
Use the perspective to assign the correct logical label.
One proposition can have multiple labels simultaneously.

میں ایک ہیں۔ مختلف اعتبارات سے اس کا نام مختلف ہو گیا ہے۔ اب اگر اس حیثیت سے دیکھیں کہ اس کے اندر صدق و کذب کا احتمال ہے تو خبر کہا جائے گا۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ مفید محکم ہے تو اخبار ہے۔ اگر دلیل کا جز ہونے کی حیثیت سے دیکھیں تو کہ کا مقدمہ ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ اسے طلب کیا جاتا ہے مطلوب ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ دلیل سے حاصل ہوئی ہے تو نتیجہ ہے ۔ اور اس حیثیت سے کہ اس کے بارے میں سوال کریں اور وہ علم میں واقع ہو تو مسئلہ ہے۔ قضیہ وغیرہ کی مثال زید قائم اس حیثیت سے کہ کھڑے ہونے کا حکم پایا جارہا ہے یہ قضیہ ہے ۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ زید قائم میں صدق و کذب کا احتمال ہے ۔ تو یہ قضیہ خبر ہے اور زید قائم سے حکم کا فائد ہورہا ہے۔ کہ زید کے لئے قیام ثابت ہے تو یہ اخبار ہے زید قائم اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ دلیل کا جز ہے مثلا زید قائم و کل قائم موجود یہ مقدمہ ہے۔ اب اس دعوی کو طلب کریں کہ قیام زید کے لئے ہے تو زید قائم مطلوب ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہ دلیل سے حاصل ہو ا یعنی مقدمات کو ترتیب دینے سے زید قائم " حاصل ہو تو یہ نتیجہ ہے۔ اصطلاح (۲) والمحكوم عليه فى القضيه : ۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ اصطلاح ثانی کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ اصطلاح ثانی کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مناطقہ کی اصطلاح میں محکوم علیہ کو موضوع کہتے ہیں اور محکوم بہ کو محمول کہتے ہیں اور مطلوب مثلاً زید قائم اس کا موضوع زید ہے یہ اصغر ہے اور محمول قائم ہے یہا کبر ہے اور دلیل بنتی ہے دو مقدموں سے تو جس مقدمہ میں اصغر ہو تو وہ صغری کہلائے گا جس میں اکبر ہو وہ کبری کہلائے گا۔ اور دونوں مقدموں میں جو چیز مکرر ہو تو وہ حد اوسط کہلاتی ہے۔ اصطلاح (۳): والاوسط اما محمول : ۔ یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ اصطلاح نمبر ۳ یعنی اشکال اربعہ کی تعریفات بیان کرنا ہے جن کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حد اوسط اگر صغریٰ کا محمول ہو اور کبری کا موضوع ہو تو تو شکل اول ہوگی اور اگر اس اک بر عکس ہو یعنی صفرئی میں موضوع اور کبری میں محمول ہو تو شکل رابع ہوگی اور اگر دونوں میں محمول ہو تو شکل ثانی اگر دونوں میں موضوع ہو تو شکل ثالث کہلائے گی۔
They are one. From different perspectives its name becomes different. Now if we look from the perspective that it contains the possibility of truth and falsehood, it is called khabar. From the perspective that it informs a judgment, it is ikhbar. If we look from the perspective of being a part of a proof, it is muqaddama. From the perspective that it is sought, it is matlub. From the perspective that it is obtained from a proof, it is natija. And from the perspective that one asks about it and it occurs in knowledge, it is mas'ala. Example of qadiyya etc.: Zaid qa'im: from the perspective that the judgment of standing is found, it is qadiyya. From the perspective that there is possibility of truth and falsehood in Zaid qa'im, this qadiyya is khabar. And from Zaid qa'im, a judgment is benefited, that standing is established for Zaid, so it is ikhbar. Zaid qa'im, from the perspective that it is part of a proof, e.g. Zaid qa'im wa kull qa'im mawjud, this is muqaddama. Now if we seek this claim that standing is for Zaid, then Zaid qa'im is matlub. And if it is obtained from a proof, i.e., by arranging the premises, Zaid qa'im is obtained, then it is natija. Terminology (2): Al-mahkum alayhi in the qadiyya. This is the second part of the text. The commentator intends to explain the second terminology. The gist of the second terminology is that in the terminology of logic, al-mahkum alayhi is called subject, and al-mahkum bihi is called predicate. And the sought, e.g. Zaid qa'im, its subject is Zaid, this is minor, and predicate is qa'im, this is major. And a proof consists of two premises: the premise in which the minor occurs is called minor premise, and the one in which the major occurs is called major premise. And the thing repeated in both premises is called middle term. Terminology (3): And the middle term is either predicate... This is the third part of the text. The commentator intends to explain terminology number 3, i.e., definitions of the four figures. The gist is that if the middle term is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise, then it is first figure. And if it is opposite to that, i.e., subject in the minor and predicate in the major, then it is fourth figure. If it is predicate in both, then second figure; if subject in both, then third figure.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a set of definitions and explanations of logical terms used in the science of logic (mantiq) as applied to usul al-fiqh. The author (the commentator on Al-Tawdih) begins by explaining that a single proposition (qadiyya) can be called by different names depending on the perspective from which it is viewed. If we consider the possibility of truth and falsehood, it is khabar (report). If we consider that it conveys a judgment, it is ikhbar (informing). If it is part of a larger proof, it is muqaddama (premise). If it is being sought to be proven, it is matlub (demand). If it is the result derived from a proof, it is natija (conclusion). If it is something questioned in knowledge, it is mas'ala (issue). The example of Zaid qa'im (Zaid is standing) is used to illustrate these different perspectives. Then the commentator introduces two technical terms from logic: اصطلاح (2) discusses the terms mahkum alayhi (subject) and mahkum bihi (predicate) in a qadiyya, noting that in logic the subject is called mawdu' and the predicate mahmul. He also introduces the terms minor (asghar) and major (akbar) and the two premises: minor premise (sughra) and major premise (kubra), and the middle term (hadd awsat). اصطلاح (3) defines the four figures of categorical syllogism (ashkal arba'a) based on the position of the middle term in the two premises. The first figure: middle term is predicate in minor and subject in major. Fourth figure: opposite (subject in minor, predicate in major). Second figure: predicate in both. Third figure: subject in both. These definitions are essential for understanding how qiyas (analogical reasoning) is structured in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
قضية (qadiyya): A proposition that carries a judgment (e.g., Zaid qa'im). It can be viewed as a report, an informing, a premise, a demand, a conclusion, or an issue depending on perspective.
خبر (khabar): A proposition considered from the perspective that it can be true or false.
مقدم (muqaddama): A proposition that serves as a part of a proof (dalil).
حد أوسط (hadd awsat): The middle term that appears in both premises of a syllogism and is eliminated in the conclusion.
شكل أول (shakl awwal): A syllogistic figure where the middle term is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise; considered the most evident form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From which perspective is a proposition called matlub?
A) When it can be true or false
B) When it is part of a proof
C) When it is sought to be proven
D) When it is derived from a proof

Key Takeaway
A single proposition takes different logical names based on the perspective: report, premise, demand, conclusion, or issue.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Syllogistic Structure: Subject, Predicate, Premises, and the Four Figures
Defining the four figures of categorical syllogism based on middle term position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a categorical syllogism into one of the four figures based on the position of the middle term.

Core Idea
The position of the middle term in the two premises determines the figure of the syllogism.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas (analogical reasoning) is often presented in the form of a syllogism. The four figures describe different arrangements of the middle term. The first figure is the most evident and is preferred. This lesson explains the definitions from the source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and predicate of the conclusion
The conclusion is the sought statement. Determine its subject (what is being talked about) and predicate (what is being said about it).
E.g., in 'Zaid is standing', subject = Zaid, predicate = standing.
2
Locate the middle term
Find the term that appears in both premises but not in the conclusion. This is the middle term (hadd awsat).
In a valid syllogism, the middle term connects the two premises.
3
Determine the position of the middle term in each premise
Check whether the middle term is the subject or the predicate in the minor premise and in the major premise.
The minor premise contains the subject of the conclusion; the major premise contains the predicate.
4
Apply the figure definitions
Use the table: If middle term is predicate in minor and subject in major → first figure. If subject in minor and predicate in major → fourth. If predicate in both → second. If subject in both → third.
Memorize these four patterns.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Applying First-Figure Syllogism to a Fiqh Ruling: Hajj is Obligatory
Applying logical terms to a fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a first-figure syllogism for a fiqh ruling by applying the logical terms (asghar, akbar, hadd awsat) and derive the conclusion.

Core Idea
A fiqh ruling can be proven by a first-figure syllogism: the middle term eliminates to yield the conclusion.

In the previous part, logical terms like minor (asghar), major (akbar), and middle term (hadd awsat) were defined. Now, the commentator applies these terms to the concrete fiqh ruling 'Hajj is obligatory' (al-Hajj wajib). By breaking the ruling into its logical components and constructing a syllogism in the first figure, the ruling is derived from two premises. This illustrates how Hanafi usul employs logical reasoning to support legal conclusions, even though in practice Hanafi qiyas often uses legal analogy based on effective cause (illa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the qadiyya and its components
The statement 'al-Hajj wajib' is a complete declarative sentence (qadiyya). Identify the subject (mawdu') as 'al-Hajj' and the predicate (mahmul) as 'wajib'.
In logical terms, the subject is the minor term (asghar) and the predicate is the major term (akbar).
2
Recognize the matlub (thing sought to be proven)
This whole statement is what we aim to prove. The subject of the matlub is the minor term, and the predicate is the major term.
3
Construct the first-figure syllogism
Supply a minor premise that includes the minor term connected to a middle term: 'al-Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver'. Supply a major premise that connects the middle term to the major term: 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib'.
The middle term must appear in both premises and be eliminated.
4
Identify the hadd awsat (middle term)
The middle term is 'commanded by the Lawgiver' (m'amur min al-shari'), as it appears in both premises but not in the conclusion.
In Hanafi qiyas, the middle term is analogous to the effective cause (illa).
5
Derive the conclusion
Eliminate the middle term. The remaining terms combine to give the conclusion: 'al-Hajj wajib'.
This shows that the conclusion follows necessarily from the premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصطلاحات مذکورہ کا اجراء مثلاً الحج واجب : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض ار مع توضیح بالمثال ہے یعنی اس مثال میں سابقہ اصطلاحات کا اجرا ہے۔ الحج واجب یہ حکم مطلوب ہے اور پورا قضیہ ہے اور الج یہ اصغر ہے محکوم علیہ اور موضوع ہے واجب محمول ہے اور محکوم یہ ہے ۔ اب الحج واجب یہ پورا جملہ مطلوب ہے مطلوب کا موضوع الحج یہ اصغر ہے اور محمول واجب اکبر ہے۔ اب اگر اس پر شکل اول سے استدلال کریں تو ( الحج مامور من الشارع وكل مامور من الشارع فهو واد اجب فلهذا الحج واجب) اب مامور من الشارع یہ حد اوسط ہے اس کو گرا دیا باقی نتیجہ نکل آیا المج واجب۔
Application of the mentioned terms, for example 'al-Hajj wajib'. This is the fourth part of the Sharh text. The purpose is illustration by example, i.e., application of the previous terms in this example. 'Al-Hajj wajib' is the sought ruling and a complete qadiyya. Al-Hajj is the minor (asghar), the subject (mahkum alayhi) and the subject (mawdu'). Wajib is the predicate (mahmul) and the mahkum. Now 'al-Hajj wajib' the whole sentence is the sought (matlub). The subject of the sought is al-Hajj which is the minor (asghar), and the predicate is wajib which is the major (akbar). Now if we perform istidlal (reasoning) by the first figure: 'al-Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory, therefore al-Hajj is obligatory.' Now 'commanded by the Lawgiver' is the middle term (hadd awsat); it is dropped and the result remains: al-Hajj wajib.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the practical application of the logical terms (subject, predicate, minor, major, middle term, first figure) to a concrete fiqh ruling: 'Hajj is obligatory (wajib)'. The commentator shows that in the qadiyya 'al-Hajj wajib', the subject (mahkum alayhi) is 'al-Hajj' (the minor), and the predicate (mahkum bihi) is 'wajib' (the major). This entire statement is the matlub (thing sought to be proven). To prove this ruling, a syllogism in the first figure is constructed: the minor premise is 'al-Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver', the major premise is 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib', and the middle term 'commanded by the Lawgiver' appears in both premises. After eliminating the middle term, the conclusion 'al-Hajj wajib' is reached. This illustrates how Hanafi usul employs logical reasoning (qiyas mantiqi) to derive or support fiqh rulings, even though in practice Hanafi qiyas often uses legal analogy rather than syllogistic form. The commentator emphasizes that the middle term is dropped, showing that the conclusion follows directly from the two premises.

Key Terms
شکل اول (shakl awwal): The first figure of syllogism where the middle term is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise.
حد اوسط (hadd awsat): The middle term that appears in both premises and is eliminated to produce the conclusion; here 'commanded by the Lawgiver'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the syllogism for 'al-Hajj wajib', what is the middle term (hadd awsat)?
A) Al-Hajj
B) Wajib
C) Mamur min al-shari'
D) Fahadha

Key Takeaway
A first-figure syllogism can prove a fiqh ruling by eliminating the middle term that connects the subject to the predicate.

Definition and Role of Qa'ida in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining 'qa'ida' as a universal premise that facilitates deriving fiqh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'qa'ida' as a universal major premise in qiyas and explain its role in tawassul ila al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A qa'ida is a universal premise that, combined with a minor premise, yields a fiqh ruling.

This passage defines 'qa'ida' as a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliya) that serves as the major premise in qiyas, facilitating the derivation of fiqh rulings. The commentator then discusses a subtle dispute between the matn author and Tarikh about whether the major premise alone or both premises together constitute the 'muwasil' (that which leads to fiqh). Understanding this definition is essential for grasping how usul al-fiqh functions as a tool for istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
Recognize that 'qa'ida' is being defined as a key concept in usul al-fiqh, specifically as a universal proposition used in analogical reasoning.
The passage is part of a sharh on Al-Tawdih.
2
Deconstruct the definition
Break down the definition: 'qa'ida' is a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliya) that serves as the major premise (kubra) in a qiyas, and its purpose is to help obtain the minor premise (sughra) easily.
The example given is 'everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib'.
3
Understand tawassul ila al-fiqh
Explain the process: combining the universal major premise with an easily obtained minor premise to actually produce a fiqh ruling.
This is the practical derivation of rulings.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on muwasil
Compare the views of Tarikh (both premises together) and the matn author (only the major premise). Note the commentator's preference and reasoning from logical necessity.
The dispute is about what exactly leads to fiqh.
5
Reflect on the broader implication
Understand that this discussion shows how usul al-fiqh includes the study of conditions and states of proofs, not just the principles themselves.
The final part of the passage emphasizes that knowledge of conditions is necessary for the qiyas to be complete.

فا القواعد : ۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ یہ بتانا ہے کہ تعریف میں قاعدہ بمعنی قضیہ کلیہ کے ہے لیکن مطلق نہیں بلکہ مرادوہ قضیہ کلیہ ہے جو مسائل فقہ پر پیش کی جانی والی دلیل کے صغری سھلتہ الحصول کے لئے کبری بنتا ہے اس کو قضیہ کلیہ کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے کہ مثال ھذا میں دعوی ہے الحج واجب دلیل۔ الحج مامور من الشارع و كل ماهو مامور من الشارع فهو واجب نتيجه - الحج واجب آيس كل ما هو مامور من الشارع فهو واجب يه كبرى قضيه کلیہ ہے اور سکھلتہ الحصول اس وجہ سے کہا کہ دلیل کا صغری تیار کرنے میں آسانی ہوتی ہے اور توصل کا معنی ہے قضیہ کلیہ کو صغری سهلة الحصول کے ساتھ اس طور پر ملانا کہ حکم فقہی قوت سے بالفعل حاصل ہو جائے (یعنی پہلے اس حکم کے پائے جانے کا امکان تھا اب وہ بالفعل پایا جائے ) یہی توصل الی الفقہ ہے۔ فائدہ:۔ تاریخ کے کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کبری کو جب صغری سھلہ الحصول سے ملا ئینگے تو دونوں کا مجموعہ موصل الی الفقہ ہے جبکہ مائن کے کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صرف کبری یا ملازمہ کلیہ یہ اصول فقہ کے قواعد کلیہ بنتے ہیں اور صرف یہی موصل الی الفقہ ہیں تو اس میں تاریخ کا قول درست ہے کیونکہ علم میزان کی اصطلاح میں دونوں کا اعتبار ہے صرف کبری موصل نہیں بن سکتا لیکن چونکہ موصل ہونے میں کبر کی عمدہ ہے اس لئے ماتن نے صرف کبری کی طرف موصل ہونے کی نسبت کر دی۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ لكن تحصيل القاعده - یہ عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ یہ ہے کہ مائن نے کہا تھا شرائط کا جاننا ضروری ہے اب شاریخ اسکی وضاحت تے ہیں کہ جب تک شرائط معلوم نہ ہوں تو یہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلیہ مکمل نہیں ہوگا تو خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ اصول فقہ میں لائل کے احوال اور شرائط وغیرہ سے بحث کرنا یہ بھی اصول فقہ کے تحت داخل ہے کوئی نئی چیز نہیں ہے قَوْلُهُ ) وَيَكُونُ الْقِيَاسُ قَدْ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأَى مُجْتَهِدٍ ) يَعْنِي يُشْتَرَطُ ذَلِكَ فِيمَا سَبَقَ فِيهِ اجْتِهَادُ الْآرَاء لِيُحْتَرَزَ بِهِ عَنْ مُخَالَفَةِ الْإِجْمَاعِ أَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ يَسْبِقُ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ اجْتِهَادٌ أَوْ سَبَقَ اجْتِهَادُ مُجْتَهِد وَاحِدٍ فَقَط فَلَا خَفَاءَ فِي جَوَازِ الِاجْتِهَادِ عَلَى خِلافِهِ .
As for the principles (al-qawa'id): This is the fifth part of the Sharh. The commentator intends to explain that in the definition, qa'ida means a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliya), but not absolutely. Rather, it refers to that universal proposition which serves as the major premise (kubra) for facilitating the attainment of the minor premise (sughra) of the proof presented for fiqh issues. This is called a universal proposition. As in this example, the claim is 'al-Hajj wajib'. The proof: 'al-Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib'. The conclusion is 'al-Hajj wajib'. So 'everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib' is a universal major premise. And 'easy attainment' is said because it facilitates preparing the minor premise of the proof. And 'tawassul' means combining the universal premise with an easily obtained minor premise in such a way that the fiqh ruling is actually obtained (i.e., previously there was possibility of the ruling, now it is actually obtained). This is tawassul ila al-fiqh. Benefit: From the statement of Tarikh it appears that when the major premise is combined with an easily obtained minor premise, then their total is what leads to fiqh (muwasil ila al-fiqh). While from the statement of the Matn (author), it appears that only the major premise or the universal concomitant (mulazima kulliya) constitutes the universal principles (qawa'id kulliya) of usul al-fiqh and only these are muwasil to fiqh. In this, the statement of Tarikh is correct because in the science of logic (mizan), both parts are considered; the major alone cannot be muwasil. However, since the major is predominant in being muwasil, the Matn attributed the leading to the major alone. And Allah knows best. But the acquisition of the principle: This is the last part of the text. The commentator intends that the Matn said it is necessary to know the conditions. Now the commentator clarifies that until the conditions are known, this major premise of the first figure and the universal concomitant (mulazima kulliya) of the exceptive syllogism will not be complete. So the summary is that discussing the states and conditions of proofs in usul al-fiqh falls under usul al-fiqh; it is not a new matter. His statement: 'And the qiyas has led to the opinion of a mujtahid' means that this is required in matters where opinions of mujtahids have preceded, to avoid contradicting consensus. As for when no ijtihad has preceded in the issue, or only the ijtihad of a single mujtahid has preceded, then there is no concealment in the permissibility of ijtihad against it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on Al-Tawdih, now focusing on the definition and role of 'qa'ida' (principle) in usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains that 'qa'ida' in this context does not mean any universal proposition, but specifically a universal proposition that serves as the major premise (kubri) in a qiyas, and which helps in easily obtaining the minor premise (sughra) for deriving a fiqh ruling. The example is again 'al-Hajj wajib', where the major premise is 'everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib'. This universal premise is called a qadiyya kulliya. The term 'tawassul ila al-fiqh' refers to the process of combining this major premise with an easily obtainable minor premise (e.g., 'al-Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver') to actually produce the fiqh ruling. Then there is a benefit (fa'ida): a discussion between two scholars, Tarikh and the matn author (Matn). Tarikh holds that the combination of both major and minor premises is the muwasil (that which leads to fiqh), while the Matn holds that only the major premise is the muwasil. The commentator sides with Tarikh, noting that in logic both parts are needed, but the Matn attributed the leading to the major because it is predominant. Finally, the commentator addresses the last part of the matn regarding the necessity of knowing conditions for the qiyas. The point is that discussing the states and conditions (ahwal wa shurut) of proofs is itself part of usul al-fiqh. The closing Arabic sentence clarifies that when a qiyas leads to a mujtahid's opinion, it is required to avoid contradicting consensus (ijma') if there is prior ijtihad on the matter. If no ijtihad has preceded, or only one mujtahid's opinion, then ijtihad against it is permissible. This is a discussion about the permissibility of ijtihad and the conditions for opposing previous ijtihad.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'ida): A universal proposition (qadiyya kulliya) that serves as the major premise in a qiyas to facilitate deriving fiqh rulings.
توصل إلى الفقه (tawassul ila al-fiqh): The process of combining a universal major premise with an easily obtained minor premise to actually produce a fiqh ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what constitutes the 'muwasil ila al-fiqh' (that which leads to fiqh)?
A) The major premise alone
B) The minor premise alone
C) Both the major and minor premises together
D) The conclusion alone

Key Takeaway
A qa'ida in Hanafi usul is a universal major premise that, when combined with an easily obtained minor premise, produces a fiqh ruling; both premises are necessary for the derivation.

The Mutawassil Debate: Exclusive to Mujtahids or Inclusive of Muqallids?
Commentary on the scope of mutawassil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the two positions on the scope of mutawassil and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
The mutawassil category is debated: is he only a mujtahid or also a muqallid? The consensus leans towards the first.

In this passage, the commentator critiques a possibility raised by the matn author regarding the mutawassil — an intermediate figure between a full mujtahid and a pure muqallid. The matn considered it 'not far' that the mutawassil could be both a mujtahid and a muqallid, but the commentator argues this is irrational. We will unpack their arguments and see why the more restrictive view is preferred, and how this affects the study of taqlid and ijtihad in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possibilities for mutawassil
State the two possibilities mentioned: (1) mutawassil is only a mujtahid, (2) mutawassil is both mujtahid and muqallid. Understand that the matn author did not outright reject the second view, only said it is 'not far'.
2
Understand the commentator's objection
The commentator argues the second view is irrational (ba'id an al-aql) because no earlier usuli (salaf) held it. This is a methodological critique: novelty without precedent is suspect in usul.
3
Analyze the responses defending the matn
Two weak responses are given: (a) it is a subtle point that only some understand, so it is not opposition to salaf; (b) even if it is far, mentioning it under the heading of 'far' is customary. Both are deemed weak by the commentator.
The passage says 'both answers are weak, as is not hidden from the intelligent.'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether the category of mutawassil includes muqallids or not. This affects how we classify students of usul and the scope of taqlid discussions in the discipline.
The passage notes that earlier usulis mentioned taqlid not because mutawassil is general, but to contrast with ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) متوصل فقط مجتہد ھو (۲) مجتہد و مقلد دونوں ہوں ۔ اور اس دوسرے احتمال کے بارے میں ماتن نے کہا تھا ولا بعد ۔ اب شارح کہتے ہیں کہ یہ دوسرا احتمال بعید از عقل ہے باقی رھا کہ کیسے بعید از عقل ہے؟ وہ اس طرح ہے کہ جتنے اصولیین گزر چکے ہیں کسی نے یہ قول اختیار نہیں کیا تو ماتن کو دھو کہ اس بات سے لگا کہ اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں تقلید کی بحث کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے یہ اس لئے ہے کہ متوصل میں تقسیم ہے حالانکہ جن اصولیین نے اپنی کتابوں میں تقلید کی بحث کو ذکر کیا ہے اس وجہ سے نہیں کیا کہ متوصل عام ہے بلکہ انہوں نے تصریح کی ہے کہ ہم نے تقلید کی مباحث کو اس لئے ذکر کیا ہے تا کہ یہ اجتہاد کے مقابل ہو جائے اور اجتہاد کی وضاحت ہو جائے کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے تعرف الاشیاء با ضد ادھا۔ فائدہ:۔ شارح کا یہ اعتراض کہ چونکہ اس کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ بعید از عقل ہے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ لطائف میں سے ایک لطیفہ ہے اور نکات میں سے ایک نکتہ ہے یہ کسی کسی کو سمجھ آتے ہیں ہر کسی کو سمجھ میں نہیں آتے اس لئے یہ مخالفت سلف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اس قبیل سے ہے کہ یہ نکتہ سلف نے بیان نہیں کیا ماتن نے ذکر کر دیا ہے اس لیے یہ بعید نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۲): واقعی یہ بعید ہے لیکن بعید کولا[؟] بعد کے عنوان سے ذکر کر نا متعارف بین العلماء ہے گو تاویل [؟] کیسا تھ ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے اس لفظ کیسا تھ [؟] کے بعد ہی کو بیان کیا ہے عدم بعد کو بیان نہیں کیا لیکن یہ دونوں جواب کمزور ہیں كما لا يخفى على المتفطن

تشریح: قوله ولا يقال : - شارح نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے متن میں کہا گیا ہے کہ متوصل جب عام ہو تو الی مسائل اللہ کہیں گے شاریخ نے وضاحت کرتے ہوئے وجہ بیان کی ہے کیونکہ فقہ نام ہے ادلہ سے احکام کو حاصل کرنے کا اور ادلہ سے احکام حاصل کرنا یہ مجتہد کا کام ہے اور مسائل جس طرح مجتہد کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی مقلد کو بھی حاصل ہوتے ہیں۔

هَذَا الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى الدَّلِيلِ وَأَمَّا بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى الْمَدْلُولِ فَإِنَّ القَضِيَّةَ المَذْكُورَةَ إِنَّمَا يُمْكِنُ الْبَاتُهَا كُلِّيَّةَ إِذَا عُرِفَ أَنْوَاعُ الْحُكْمِ وَأَنَّ أَيَّ نَوْعٍ مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ يَعْمُتُ بِأَى نَوْعٍ مِنْ الْأَدِلَّةِ بِخُصُوصِيَّةٍ نَاشِئَةٍ مِنْ الْحُكْمِ كَكَوْنِ هَذَا الشَّيْءِ عِلَّةً لِذَلِكَ فَإِنَّ هَذَا الْحُكْمَ لَا يُمْكِنُ الْبَاتُهُ بِالْقِيَاسِ، ثُمَّ الْمَبَاحِثُ المُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِالمَحْكُوم بِهِ، وَهُوَ فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ كَكَوْنِهِ عِبَادَةً أَوْ عُقُوبَةً وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ الْمَبَاحِثُ المُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِالْمَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ، وَهُوَ الْمُكَلَّفُ وَمَعْرِفَةُ الأهْلِيَّةِ وَالْعَوَارِضِ الَّتِي تَعْرِضُ عَلَى الأهْلِيَّةِ سَمَاوِيَّةٌ وَمُكْتَسَبَةً مُنْدَرِجَةٌ تَحْتَ تِلْكَ القَضِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ أَيْضًا لِاخْتِلَافِ الْأَحْكَامِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى وُجُودِ الْعَوَارِضِ وَعَدَمِهَا فَيَكُونُ تَرْكِيبُ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى إِثْبَاتِ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ هَكَذَا: هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ حَكُمْ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِفِعْلٍ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ، وَهَذَا الْفِعْلُ صَادِرٌ مِنْ مُكَلَّفٍ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ، وَلَمْ تُوجَدِ الْعَوَارِضُ الْمَانِعَةُ مِنْ ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ وَيَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ قِيَاسٌ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ. هَذَا هُوَ الصُّغْرَى، ثُمَّ الْكُبْرَى قَوْلُنَا: وَكُلُّ حُكْمٍ مَوْصُوفٍ بِالصِّفَاتِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ الْمَوْصُوفُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ. فَهَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةُ الْأَخِيرَةُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَبِطَرِيقِ الْمُلَازَمَةِ هَكَذَا: كُلَّمَا وُجِدَ قِيَاسٌ مَوْصُوفٌ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ دَالٌّ عَلَى حُكْمٍ مَوْصُوفٍ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ يَثْبُتُ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ لَكِنَّهُ وُجِدَ الْقِيَاسُ الْمَوْصُوفُ إِلَخُ فَعُلِمَ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ الْمَبَاحِثِ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةِ مُنْدَرِجَةٌ تَحْتَ تِلْكَ الْقَضِيَّةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَيِ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ، فَهَذَا هُوَ مَعْنَى التَّوَصُّلِ الْقَرِيبِ الْمَذْكُورِ. وَإِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ مَسَائِلِ الْأُصُولِ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى قَوْلِنَا: كُلُّ حُكْمٍ كَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ دَلِيلٌ كَذَا فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ أَوْ كُلَّمَا وُجِدَ دَلِيلٌ كَذَا دَالٌّ عَلَى حُكْمٍ كَذَا يَثْبُتُ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ. عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ يُبْحَثُ فِي هَذَا الْعِلْمِ عَنِ الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْأُولَى مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلثَّانِيَةِ وَالثَّانِيَةُ ثَابِتَةٌ بِالْأُولَى، وَالْمَبَاحِثُ الَّتِي تَرْجِعُ إِلَى أَنَّ الْأُولَى مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلثَّانِيَةِ وَالثَّانِيَةُ ثَابِتَةٌ بِالْأُولَى بَعْضُهَا نَاشِئَةٌ عَنِ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَبَعْضُهَا نَاشِئَةٌ عَنْ
There are two possibilities: (1) The mutawassil is only a mujtahid. (2) Both mujtahid and muqallid. Regarding the second possibility, the matn said 'and no far'. Now the commentator says that this second possibility is irrational. As for how it is irrational, it is because no usuli who passed has chosen this saying. So the matn (author) grasped that the discussion of taqlid is mentioned in usul al-fiqh books because mutawassil is divided, whereas those usulis who mentioned taqlid did not do so because mutawassil is general, but they stated that they mentioned taqlid to contrast with ijtihad and clarify ijtihad, because the principle is: things are known by their opposites. Benefit: The commentator's objection that since no one holds it, it is irrational, is incorrect because it is a subtlety and a point that only some understand, so it is not opposition to the salaf; rather it is of the type that the salaf did not mention, and the matn mentioned it, so it is not far. Second answer: It is indeed far, but mentioning it under the heading of 'far' is customary among scholars, even if it requires interpretation. The summary is that the matn mentioned 'not far' after the word 'far', but both answers are weak, as is not hidden from the intelligent.

Commentary: His saying 'and it is not said': The commentator explained the text. The text said that when mutawassil is general, they will say 'to the issues of Allah'. The commentator clarified the reason because fiqh is the acquisition of rulings from evidences, and acquiring rulings from evidences is the work of the mujtahid, and the muqallid also acquires issues just as the mujtahid does.

What we have mentioned is with respect to the evidence. As for with respect to the indicated (the ruling), the aforementioned proposition can be universal only if the types of rulings are known and which type of ruling is established by which type of evidence due to a specificity arising from the ruling, such as something being a cause for that, for that ruling cannot be established by qiyas. Then the discussions related to the subject of the ruling (mahkum bih), which is the act of the mukallaf, such as it being worship or punishment and the like. Then the discussions related to the person under obligation (mahkum alayh), which is the mukallaf, and knowledge of legal capacity and the impediments that affect capacity, whether divinely ordained or acquired, are also subsumed under that universal proposition because rulings differ with the difference of the person under obligation based on the presence or absence of impediments. So the construction of the proof for establishing fiqh issues in the first form is: This ruling is established because it is a ruling of this nature related to an act of this nature, and this act originates from a mukallaf of this nature, and the preventing impediments do not exist, and a qiyas of this nature indicates the establishment of this ruling. This is the minor premise. Then the major premise is our saying: Every ruling described with the mentioned attributes, an analogy described as such indicates its establishment, so it is established. This last proposition is from the issues of usul al-fiqh, and by way of implication: Whenever an analogy described with these attributes is found indicating a ruling described with these attributes, that ruling is established. But the described analogy is found, etc. So it is known that all the preceding discussions are subsumed under that mentioned universal proposition, which is one of the two premises of the proof for fiqh issues. This is the meaning of the mentioned 'qarib al-tawassul' (close intermediate). And when it is known that all issues of usul return to our saying: Every ruling of such type, a proof of such type indicates its establishment, so it is established; or whenever a proof of such type is found indicating a ruling of such type, that ruling is established. It is known that in this science, we investigate the shariah proofs and universal rulings insofar as the first establishes the second and the second is established by the first. And the discussions that return to the fact that the first establishes the second and the second is established by the first, some of them arise from the proofs and some arise from...
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the scope of the mutawassil (the intermediate category between mujtahid and muqallid) and on the general proposition that subsumes all discussions of usul al-fiqh. The commentator begins by discussing two possibilities for the mutawassil: that he is only a mujtahid, or that he is both mujtahid and muqallid. The matn (original text) had said that the second possibility is 'not far' (la bu'd), but the commentator (sharh) argues that it is irrational because no earlier usuli held that view. The commentator then provides a benefit (fa'idah) defending the matn, noting that this is a subtle point that the salaf did not mention, so it is not an innovation. Two weak answers are given, and the commentator concludes that the matn's mention of 'la bu'd' after 'bu'd' is a customary usage among scholars, but the answers are weak. The commentary then turns to a wider methodological point: the study of usul al-fiqh revolves around a universal proposition that links proofs to rulings. The author explains that the proposition can be universal only when the types of rulings and their specific relations to proofs are known. He then breaks down the construction of a proof for a fiqh ruling into a syllogism: a minor premise stating that a particular ruling (with specific attributes) is indicated by a specific qiyas, and a major premise that any ruling with those attributes is established by such qiyas. This major premise is itself a principle of usul al-fiqh. All discussions—whether about the act of the mukallaf (mahkum bih) or the person under obligation (mahkum alayh) including capacity and impediments—are subsumed under this universal proposition. This is the meaning of 'qarib al-tawassul' (close connection). The passage concludes that all issues of usul al-fiqh are reducible to one of two forms: (1) Every ruling of a certain type is established by a certain type of proof, or (2) Whenever a certain type of proof indicates a certain ruling, that ruling is established. Thus, the science investigates proofs and universal rulings from the perspective that proofs establish rulings and rulings are established by proofs.

Key Terms
متوصل (mutawassil): An intermediate category between a mujtahid and a muqallid; one who has some ability in ijtihad but not full.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar who performs ijtihad to derive rulings from the sources.
مقلد (muqallid): A person who follows a mujtahid without independent derivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the mutawassil debate?
A) It changes the number of proofs required for ijtihad.
B) It determines whether the category of mutawassil includes muqallids or not, affecting the scope of taqlid discussions.
C) It affects the validity of qiyas.
D) It determines whether usul al-fiqh is a universal science.

Key Takeaway
The mutawassil is best understood as a mujtahid; the view that he is also a muqallid is considered irrational by the commentator due to lack of precedent.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
The Universal Proposition of Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs and Rulings
Explanation of the universal proposition of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the universal proposition of usul al-fiqh (qadiyya kulliyya) and construct the syllogism that establishes any fiqh ruling through qiyas.

Core Idea
All usul al-fiqh reduces to one universal proposition: a ruling of type X is established by a proof of type Y.

The second part of this passage moves from a specific debate about the mutawassil to a grand methodological claim: all discussions in usul al-fiqh are subsumed under a single universal proposition. This proposition, when combined with knowledge of the types of rulings and proofs, forms the backbone of juristic reasoning. The author illustrates how to structure a proof as a syllogism (minor premise + major premise) and shows that this structure underlies the entire discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal proposition
The passage states: "Every ruling of such type, a proof of such type indicates its establishment, so it is established; or whenever a proof of such type indicating a ruling of such type is found, that ruling is established." This is the qadiyya kulliyya.
Think of it as a template: if the attributes of the ruling match the attributes of the proof (qiyas), then the ruling is established.
2
Understand the conditions for universality
The proposition can be universal only when we know the types of rulings (e.g., worship, punishment) and which type of proof (e.g., qiyas with a specific illa) applies to each. The passage gives an example: a ruling that is a cause (illa) for something else cannot be established by qiyas (because qiyas itself relies on illa).
This ensures the proposition is not applied blindly; context matters.
3
See how related discussions are subsumed
All discussions about the mahkum bih (the act of the mukallaf) and the mahkum alayh (the mukallaf himself, including capacity and impediments) are subsumed under the universal proposition because rulings differ based on attributes of the act and the person.
The passage explicitly says these are 'also subsumed'.
4
Construct the syllogism (minor and major premise)
The minor premise (sughra) describes the specific case: "This ruling (with attributes) is related to an act (with attributes) from a mukallaf (with attributes), no impediments, and a qiyas (with attributes) indicates it." The major premise (kubra) is the universal proposition itself. The conclusion is the ruling's establishment.
The passage calls this the 'first form' of proof structure.
5
Conclude with the meaning of 'qarib al-tawassul'
The term 'qarib al-tawassul' (close intermediate) refers to the fact that all usul discussions are directly linked to this universal proposition. The entire science of usul is about understanding proofs and rulings as described.

Source Text

میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) متوصل فقط مجتہد ھو (۲) مجتہد و مقلد دونوں ہوں ۔ اور اس دوسرے احتمال کے بارے میں ماتن نے کہا تھا ولا بعد ۔ اب شارح کہتے ہیں کہ یہ دوسرا احتمال بعید از عقل ہے باقی رھا کہ کیسے بعید از عقل ہے؟ وہ اس طرح ہے کہ جتنے اصولیین گزر چکے ہیں کسی نے یہ قول اختیار نہیں کیا تو ماتن کو دھو کہ اس بات سے لگا کہ اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں تقلید کی بحث کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے یہ اس لئے ہے کہ متوصل میں تقسیم ہے حالانکہ جن اصولیین نے اپنی کتابوں میں تقلید کی بحث کو ذکر کیا ہے اس وجہ سے نہیں کیا کہ متوصل عام ہے بلکہ انہوں نے تصریح کی ہے کہ ہم نے تقلید کی مباحث کو اس لئے ذکر کیا ہے تا کہ یہ اجتہاد کے مقابل ہو جائے اور اجتہاد کی وضاحت ہو جائے کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے تعرف الاشیاء با ضد ادھا۔ فائدہ:۔ شارح کا یہ اعتراض کہ چونکہ اس کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ بعید از عقل ہے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ لطائف میں سے ایک لطیفہ ہے اور نکات میں سے ایک نکتہ ہے یہ کسی کسی کو سمجھ آتے ہیں ہر کسی کو سمجھ میں نہیں آتے اس لئے یہ مخالفت سلف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اس قبیل سے ہے کہ یہ نکتہ سلف نے بیان نہیں کیا ماتن نے ذکر کر دیا ہے اس لیے یہ بعید نہیں ہے۔ جواب (۲): واقعی یہ بعید ہے لیکن بعید کولا[؟] بعد کے عنوان سے ذکر کر نا متعارف بین العلماء ہے گو تاویل [؟] کیسا تھ ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے اس لفظ کیسا تھ [؟] کے بعد ہی کو بیان کیا ہے عدم بعد کو بیان نہیں کیا لیکن یہ دونوں جواب کمزور ہیں كما لا يخفى على المتفطن

تشریح: قوله ولا يقال : - شارح نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے متن میں کہا گیا ہے کہ متوصل جب عام ہو تو الی مسائل اللہ کہیں گے شاریخ نے وضاحت کرتے ہوئے وجہ بیان کی ہے کیونکہ فقہ نام ہے ادلہ سے احکام کو حاصل کرنے کا اور ادلہ سے احکام حاصل کرنا یہ مجتہد کا کام ہے اور مسائل جس طرح مجتہد کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی مقلد کو بھی حاصل ہوتے ہیں۔

هَذَا الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى الدَّلِيلِ وَأَمَّا بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى الْمَدْلُولِ فَإِنَّ القَضِيَّةَ المَذْكُورَةَ إِنَّمَا يُمْكِنُ الْبَاتُهَا كُلِّيَّةَ إِذَا عُرِفَ أَنْوَاعُ الْحُكْمِ وَأَنَّ أَيَّ نَوْعٍ مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ يَعْمُتُ بِأَى نَوْعٍ مِنْ الْأَدِلَّةِ بِخُصُوصِيَّةٍ نَاشِئَةٍ مِنْ الْحُكْمِ كَكَوْنِ هَذَا الشَّيْءِ عِلَّةً لِذَلِكَ فَإِنَّ هَذَا الْحُكْمَ لَا يُمْكِنُ الْبَاتُهُ بِالْقِيَاسِ، ثُمَّ الْمَبَاحِثُ المُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِالمَحْكُوم بِهِ، وَهُوَ فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ كَكَوْنِهِ عِبَادَةً أَوْ عُقُوبَةً وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ الْمَبَاحِثُ المُتَعَلَّقَةُ بِالْمَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ، وَهُوَ الْمُكَلَّفُ وَمَعْرِفَةُ الأهْلِيَّةِ وَالْعَوَارِضِ الَّتِي تَعْرِضُ عَلَى الأهْلِيَّةِ سَمَاوِيَّةٌ وَمُكْتَسَبَةً مُنْدَرِجَةٌ تَحْتَ تِلْكَ القَضِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ أَيْضًا لِاخْتِلَافِ الْأَحْكَامِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى وُجُودِ الْعَوَارِضِ وَعَدَمِهَا فَيَكُونُ تَرْكِيبُ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى إِثْبَاتِ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ هَكَذَا: هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ حَكُمْ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِفِعْلٍ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ، وَهَذَا الْفِعْلُ صَادِرٌ مِنْ مُكَلَّفٍ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ، وَلَمْ تُوجَدِ الْعَوَارِضُ الْمَانِعَةُ مِنْ ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ وَيَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ قِيَاسٌ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ. هَذَا هُوَ الصُّغْرَى، ثُمَّ الْكُبْرَى قَوْلُنَا: وَكُلُّ حُكْمٍ مَوْصُوفٍ بِالصِّفَاتِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ الْمَوْصُوفُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ. فَهَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةُ الْأَخِيرَةُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَبِطَرِيقِ الْمُلَازَمَةِ هَكَذَا: كُلَّمَا وُجِدَ قِيَاسٌ مَوْصُوفٌ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ دَالٌّ عَلَى حُكْمٍ مَوْصُوفٍ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ يَثْبُتُ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ لَكِنَّهُ وُجِدَ الْقِيَاسُ الْمَوْصُوفُ إِلَخُ فَعُلِمَ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ الْمَبَاحِثِ الْمُتَقَدِّمَةِ مُنْدَرِجَةٌ تَحْتَ تِلْكَ الْقَضِيَّةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَيِ الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ، فَهَذَا هُوَ مَعْنَى التَّوَصُّلِ الْقَرِيبِ الْمَذْكُورِ. وَإِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ مَسَائِلِ الْأُصُولِ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى قَوْلِنَا: كُلُّ حُكْمٍ كَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ دَلِيلٌ كَذَا فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ أَوْ كُلَّمَا وُجِدَ دَلِيلٌ كَذَا دَالٌّ عَلَى حُكْمٍ كَذَا يَثْبُتُ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ. عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ يُبْحَثُ فِي هَذَا الْعِلْمِ عَنِ الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْأُولَى مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلثَّانِيَةِ وَالثَّانِيَةُ ثَابِتَةٌ بِالْأُولَى، وَالْمَبَاحِثُ الَّتِي تَرْجِعُ إِلَى أَنَّ الْأُولَى مُثْبِتَةٌ لِلثَّانِيَةِ وَالثَّانِيَةُ ثَابِتَةٌ بِالْأُولَى بَعْضُهَا نَاشِئَةٌ عَنِ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَبَعْضُهَا نَاشِئَةٌ عَنْ
There are two possibilities: (1) The mutawassil is only a mujtahid. (2) Both mujtahid and muqallid. Regarding the second possibility, the matn said 'and no far'. Now the commentator says that this second possibility is irrational. As for how it is irrational, it is because no usuli who passed has chosen this saying. So the matn (author) grasped that the discussion of taqlid is mentioned in usul al-fiqh books because mutawassil is divided, whereas those usulis who mentioned taqlid did not do so because mutawassil is general, but they stated that they mentioned taqlid to contrast with ijtihad and clarify ijtihad, because the principle is: things are known by their opposites. Benefit: The commentator's objection that since no one holds it, it is irrational, is incorrect because it is a subtlety and a point that only some understand, so it is not opposition to the salaf; rather it is of the type that the salaf did not mention, and the matn mentioned it, so it is not far. Second answer: It is indeed far, but mentioning it under the heading of 'far' is customary among scholars, even if it requires interpretation. The summary is that the matn mentioned 'not far' after the word 'far', but both answers are weak, as is not hidden from the intelligent.

Commentary: His saying 'and it is not said': The commentator explained the text. The text said that when mutawassil is general, they will say 'to the issues of Allah'. The commentator clarified the reason because fiqh is the acquisition of rulings from evidences, and acquiring rulings from evidences is the work of the mujtahid, and the muqallid also acquires issues just as the mujtahid does.

What we have mentioned is with respect to the evidence. As for with respect to the indicated (the ruling), the aforementioned proposition can be universal only if the types of rulings are known and which type of ruling is established by which type of evidence due to a specificity arising from the ruling, such as something being a cause for that, for that ruling cannot be established by qiyas. Then the discussions related to the subject of the ruling (mahkum bih), which is the act of the mukallaf, such as it being worship or punishment and the like. Then the discussions related to the person under obligation (mahkum alayh), which is the mukallaf, and knowledge of legal capacity and the impediments that affect capacity, whether divinely ordained or acquired, are also subsumed under that universal proposition because rulings differ with the difference of the person under obligation based on the presence or absence of impediments. So the construction of the proof for establishing fiqh issues in the first form is: This ruling is established because it is a ruling of this nature related to an act of this nature, and this act originates from a mukallaf of this nature, and the preventing impediments do not exist, and a qiyas of this nature indicates the establishment of this ruling. This is the minor premise. Then the major premise is our saying: Every ruling described with the mentioned attributes, an analogy described as such indicates its establishment, so it is established. This last proposition is from the issues of usul al-fiqh, and by way of implication: Whenever an analogy described with these attributes is found indicating a ruling described with these attributes, that ruling is established. But the described analogy is found, etc. So it is known that all the preceding discussions are subsumed under that mentioned universal proposition, which is one of the two premises of the proof for fiqh issues. This is the meaning of the mentioned 'qarib al-tawassul' (close intermediate). And when it is known that all issues of usul return to our saying: Every ruling of such type, a proof of such type indicates its establishment, so it is established; or whenever a proof of such type is found indicating a ruling of such type, that ruling is established. It is known that in this science, we investigate the shariah proofs and universal rulings insofar as the first establishes the second and the second is established by the first. And the discussions that return to the fact that the first establishes the second and the second is established by the first, some of them arise from the proofs and some arise from...
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the scope of the mutawassil (the intermediate category between mujtahid and muqallid) and on the general proposition that subsumes all discussions of usul al-fiqh. The commentator begins by discussing two possibilities for the mutawassil: that he is only a mujtahid, or that he is both mujtahid and muqallid. The matn (original text) had said that the second possibility is 'not far' (la bu'd), but the commentator (sharh) argues that it is irrational because no earlier usuli held that view. The commentator then provides a benefit (fa'idah) defending the matn, noting that this is a subtle point that the salaf did not mention, so it is not an innovation. Two weak answers are given, and the commentator concludes that the matn's mention of 'la bu'd' after 'bu'd' is a customary usage among scholars, but the answers are weak. The commentary then turns to a wider methodological point: the study of usul al-fiqh revolves around a universal proposition that links proofs to rulings. The author explains that the proposition can be universal only when the types of rulings and their specific relations to proofs are known. He then breaks down the construction of a proof for a fiqh ruling into a syllogism: a minor premise stating that a particular ruling (with specific attributes) is indicated by a specific qiyas, and a major premise that any ruling with those attributes is established by such qiyas. This major premise is itself a principle of usul al-fiqh. All discussions—whether about the act of the mukallaf (mahkum bih) or the person under obligation (mahkum alayh) including capacity and impediments—are subsumed under this universal proposition. This is the meaning of 'qarib al-tawassul' (close connection). The passage concludes that all issues of usul al-fiqh are reducible to one of two forms: (1) Every ruling of a certain type is established by a certain type of proof, or (2) Whenever a certain type of proof indicates a certain ruling, that ruling is established. Thus, the science investigates proofs and universal rulings from the perspective that proofs establish rulings and rulings are established by proofs.

Key Terms
قضية كلية (qadiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that subsumes all specific discussions in usul al-fiqh (the linkage between proofs and rulings).
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; a method of deriving a ruling for a new case based on an original case due to a common effective cause (illa).
محكوم به (mahkum bih): The subject of the ruling; the act of the mukallaf that is classified as wajib, haram, etc.
محكوم عليه (mahkum alayh): The person under obligation; the mukallaf who must perform or avoid the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the 'first form' of proof construction for establishing fiqh issues?
A) A single premise stating the ruling directly from the Quran.
B) A syllogism with a minor premise describing the specific case and a major premise being the universal proposition.
C) A chain of narrations (isnad) for each ruling.
D) An inductive listing of all similar cases.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is unified by a universal proposition: a ruling is established when its attributes match those of a valid proof, forming the core of juristic reasoning.

Four Conditions of the Mahkum Bih for a Valid Qiyas
Lists four conditions for the madlul (ruling) in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four conditions related to the mahkum bih that must be satisfied for a general proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) to be valid in Hanafi usul, and apply each condition to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A qiyas is sound only if you know the type of ruling, the act, the person, and the accidents affecting the ruling.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, constructing a valid analogical argument (qiyas) requires satisfying conditions on both the evidence (dalil) and the ruling (madlul/hukm). This lesson focuses on the four conditions related to the mahkum bih—the subject of the ruling—as explained by the commentator on the matn. These conditions ensure that the general proposition serving as the major premise in qiyas is correctly formulated.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish dalil conditions from madlul conditions
The passage notes that earlier the author gave conditions for the dalil (evidence: no abrogation, no equal/stronger counter-evidence). Now we turn to conditions for the madlul (the ruling). Know this division.
This sets the context for the four conditions that follow.
2
Understand the first condition: knowing the types of hukm (anwa' al-hukm)
The author lists six types of rulings: wujub, nadb, ibaha, etc. Also, each type must be proven by its appropriate evidence (e.g., fard from qat'i text, sunnah from mashhur or ijma, 'illah from text not qiyas).
Not every ruling type is proven by every evidence type.
3
Understand the second and third conditions: knowing the mahkum bih and mahkum alayh
The mahkum bih is the act of the mukallaf; one must know whether it is halal or haram, worship or punishment. The mahkum alayh is the mukallaf; rulings differ with the person's state (traveler, resident, free, slave).
The act and the person both affect the ruling.
4
Understand the fourth condition: knowing the 'awarid (accidents)
'Awarid are circumstances that change the ruling, such as travel (acquired) or illness (heavenly). One must know how they affect the ruling.
E.g., the rulings for a sick person differ from a healthy one.

Source Text

فيكون تركيب الدليل: - ماتن نے خلاصہ بیان کیا کہ ان امور اربعہ کا احاطہ کرنے سے دلیل کی صورت بطور قیاس
Statement of the conditions of the mahkum bih. Explanation: The author (matn) previously stated that the general proposition and the major premise of the first figure have several conditions: that the evidence is not abrogated, that there is no equal opposing evidence, no preponderant opposing evidence, and if proven by qiyas, it must not contradict the qiyas of earlier mujtahids. These pertain to the evidence. Now he mentions conditions regarding the madlul (ruling). They are as follows: (1) Knowing the types of rulings is necessary, and they are six: wujub, nadb, ibaha, etc. Second, knowing which type of ruling is proven by which type of evidence; e.g., fard is proven by decisive text, istihbab and sunnah by mashhur report or ijma. 'Illah is not proven by qiyas but by text. This is necessary because not every type of ruling is known from every type of evidence. (2) Knowing the mahkum bih, which is the act of the mukallaf; i.e., knowing whether the act is halal or haram, whether it belongs to the category of worship or punishment. Knowing this is necessary because when acts change, the ruling changes. (3) Knowing the mahkum alayh, who is the mukallaf himself. This is necessary because rulings differ with the difference of mukallafin; e.g., the rulings for a traveler are different from a resident, and for a free man and a slave. (4) Similarly, knowing the 'awarid is necessary because rulings change with differing 'awarid; 'awarid may be acquired like travel, or heavenly like illness. Knowing this is necessary because rulings change with 'awarid; e.g., the rulings for a sick person are different from a healthy one, and for a resident and a traveler. Until these things are known, the general proposition is not valid in terms of evidence. "Then the composition of the evidence: The author summarized that encompassing these four matters, the form of the evidence as qiyas...
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions related to the mahkum bih (the subject of the ruling) for the general proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) used in analogical reasoning. The author first notes that earlier conditions applied to the dalil (evidence). Now four conditions apply to the madlul (ruling). First, know the types of hukm (wujub, nadb, ibaha, etc.) and which evidence proves which type (e.g., fard from qat'i text, sunnah from mashhur or ijma). Second, know the mahkum bih itself, i.e., the act of the mukallaf and its category (worship vs punishment). Third, know the mahkum alayh, the mukallaf, because rulings differ with the person (traveler vs resident, free vs slave). Fourth, know the 'awarid (accidents) that affect the ruling, such as travel or illness. The passage concludes that without these, the general proposition is not valid. This is a classic Hanafi usul exposition on the preconditions for istinbat via qiyas.

Key Terms
المحكوم به (al-mahkūm bihī): The subject of the ruling; the act of the mukallaf that is judged (e.g., prayer as wajib).
المحكوم عليه (al-mahkūm ʿalayhi): The person upon whom the ruling applies; the mukallaf.
العوارض (al-ʿawāriḍ): Accidents that affect the mukallaf's capacity, like travel, illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A valid qiyas requires not only a sound dalil but also proper knowledge of the ruling's type, the act, the person, and the affecting accidents.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
