Are Shari Proofs Real Causes or Indicators?
Resolving the status of shari proofs as real causes or mere indicators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that shari proofs are amarat (indicators) not ilal haqiqiyya (real causes), and apply the definition of dalil to analyse the epistemological status of qiyas.

Core Idea
Shari proofs indicate rulings; they do not create them.

This lesson unpacks a foundational debate in Hanafi usul: are the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) real causes that produce rulings, or merely indicators that lead us to know rulings that already exist? The correct answer shapes how we understand the certainty of rulings derived by qiyas and the nature of divine command. The passage from Sharh al-Tawdih clarifies the Hanafi stance and addresses a theological objection about the eternal speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the core question? Are shari proofs real causes (ilal haqiqiyya) that positively affirm rulings, or are they mere indicators (amarat) that lead to knowledge of rulings?
The dispute has epistemological and theological implications.
2
Define 'dalil'
According to the text, a dalil gives knowledge of the existence of something, not the actual existence. Distinguish between 'ilm (knowledge) and wujud (existence). This definition undercuts the claim that proofs cause rulings.
External causes produce actual existence; proofs only reveal it.
3
Analyse the two interpretations of 'hukm'
If hukm is the eternal speech (khatab Allah), its thubut (establishment) means knowledge of its existence, not its actual existence. If hukm is the effect (obligation, prohibition), then proofs (except qiyas) establish it, but qiyas only reveals it.
The eternal speech cannot be 'established' by contingent proofs.
4
Examine the role of qiyas
Qiyas provides preponderant (rajih) knowledge, not certainty. It is a revealer (muzhir) of hukm, not an affirmer (muthbit). This affects the level of certainty in rulings derived by analogy.
Contrast with the first three proofs which yield decisive (jazm) knowledge.
5
Resolve the objection from Sahib al-Tawdih
The objector claims that the first three proofs were called 'usul mutlaqa' (absolute principles) that affirm rulings. The Hanafi response: thubut here means knowledge of the ruling, not its actual existence. This preserves the eternality of divine speech.
Key move: distinguish between ontological and epistemological thubut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ادله شرعیہ احکام کے لئے ملل حقیقیہ ہیں یا امارات قوله ان اريد بالحكم صاحب توضیح نے فرمایا تھا کہ حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو تو اس سے مراد ثبوت بعلمنا ہوگا اور اگر حکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب ہو تو اس سے مراد غلبہ کن ہو گا اس پر شاریخ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سوال کے جواب کی بنیاد اس بات پر ہے کہ ادلہ شرعیہ عمل حقیقیہ ہوں یعنی مثبت للاحکام ہوں حالانکہ جتنی بھی ادلہ شرعیہ ہیں وہ معرفات اور امارات ہیں احکام پر کوئی علت و دلیل مثبت للا حکام نہیں ہے۔ اور ثانیا کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی درجہ میں تسلیم کر لیں کہ اولہ شرعیہ عمل حقیقیہ ہیں تو پھر ہم پوچھیں گے کہ دلیل کا کیا معنی ہے؟ دلیل کہتے ہیں جو کسی شئی کے ثبوت کے علم کا فائدہ دے دلیل کا یہ معنی نہیں ہے کہ مئی کے نفس ثبوت کا فائدہ دے کیونکہ نفس ثبوت تو علل خارجیہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے جبکہ دلیل کہتے ہیں جس سے کسی شئے کے ثبوت یا انتفا کا فائدہ حاصل ہو جائے۔ اب ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ کوئی فرق نہیں ہے حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو یا حکم بمعنی ماشبت بالخطاب ہو دونوں صورتوں میں حکم کے ثبوت کا علم ہوگا۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہیں گے کہ علم معنی اور اک کے ہے اور اس میں تقسیم ہے خواہ ادراک جازم ہو یا راج ہو۔ جازم ہوگا ادلہ ثلاثہ کے اعتبار سے اور رائج ہوگا قیاس کے اعتبار سے جیسا کہ صاحب توضیح نے دوسرے سوال کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا تھا کہ ادراک میں تعمیم ہے خواہ ادراک جازم ہو یا اور اک راج ہوتا کہ یہ قیاس کو شامل ہو جائے ۔ باقی شاریخ کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اگر حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو تو ثبوت بعلمنا مراد لیتا اورحکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب ہو تو نفس ثبوت مراد لینا یہ تفرقہ صحیح نہیں۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ ادلہ اربعہ علامات اور امارات ہیں لیکن بظاہر ماتن کا اعتراض درست معلوم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ماقبل میں آپ نے خود ہی کہا تھا کہ اصول اربعہ میں سے پہلے تین اصول اصول مطلقہ ہیں مثبت للا حکام ہونے کی وجہ سے تو معلوم ہوا کہ حکم ان دلائل سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ تو اس پر معترض کا اعتراض ظاہر الوقوع ہے کہ حکم سے مراد نفس خطاب ہے تو مثبت بھذہ الادلہ کہنا صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ حکم بمعنی الخطاب قدیم ہے اور قدیم ثابت نہیں ہوسکتا ورنہ ان کا حادث ہونا لازم آئے گا اس اعتراض کو دفع کرنے کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ ثبوت حکم سے مراد ثبوت العلم بالحکم لیا جاوے کیونکہ ثبوت علم القدیم بالا دلہ میں کوئی حرج نہیں اور اگر حکم سے مراد اثر خطاب یعنی وجوب حرمت وغیرہ ہو تو پھر ان کا ثبوت ادلہ ثلاثہ سے تو صحیح ہے لیکن قیاس سے ثبوت صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ مثبت حکم نہیں بلکہ مظہر حکم ہے۔
Shari proofs: Are they real causes of rulings or indicators? His statement: 'If by hukm is meant...' Sahib al-Tawdih had said that if hukm is taken as the speech of Allah, then its meaning is thubut bi-'ilmuna (knowledge of its existence), and if hukm is taken as what is established by the speech, then its meaning is ghulaba (overwhelming assumption). Upon this, the commentator says: The basis of answering this question is whether the shari proofs are real causes, i.e., positive affirmers of rulings. However, all shari proofs are identifiers and indicators; there is no cause or proof that positively affirms rulings. Secondly, he says: If we concede to some degree that the shari proofs are real causes, then we ask: what is the meaning of 'dalil'? Dalil is that which gives benefit of knowledge of the existence of something. It does not mean to give benefit of the actual existence of the thing, because actual existence is known through external causes. Dalil is that from which benefit of existence or non-existence of something is obtained. So we say that there is no difference whether hukm is taken as the speech of Allah or as what is established by the speech; in both cases, we have knowledge of the existence of the hukm. At most we can say that knowledge is of two meanings: either decisive perception or preponderant. Decisive is from the three proofs, and preponderant is from analogy, as Sahib al-Tawdih said in answering the second question that perception is general, whether decisive or preponderant, so that it includes analogy. The rest of the commentator's aim is that if hukm is taken as the speech of Allah, then thubut bi-'ilmuna is meant, and if hukm is taken as what is established by the speech, then actual thubut is meant. This distinction is not correct. Response: We accept that the four proofs are signs and indicators, but apparently the objection of the matn is valid because previously you yourself said that the first three of the four principles are absolute principles due to being affirmers of rulings, so it is understood that the hukm is established from these proofs. Thus the objector's objection is apparent: if by hukm is meant the actual speech, then saying 'established by these proofs' is not correct because hukm as speech is eternal and an eternal thing cannot be established, otherwise it would necessitate its temporality. To repel this objection, it is necessary that by 'thubut al-hukm' is meant 'thubut al-ilm bi-hukm' (knowledge of the ruling), because there is no harm in knowledge of the eternal being based on proofs. And if by hukm is meant the effect of speech, i.e., obligation, prohibition etc., then their thubut from the three proofs is correct, but from analogy it is not correct because analogy is not an affirmer of hukm but rather a revealer of hukm.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage tackles a thorny issue: whether the shari proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) are real causes (ilal haqiqiyya) that produce the rulings or merely indicators (amarat) that lead to knowledge of the rulings. The commentator begins by referencing a previous distinction by Sahib al-Tawdih who said that if 'hukm' is interpreted as the speech of Allah (khatab Allah), then its thubut (establishment) is in our knowledge; if it is interpreted as what is established by the speech (ma thabata bi'l-khitab), then its thubut is real existence. The commentator argues that the answer to this depends on whether the proofs are real causes. He firmly states that all shari proofs are only identifiers (mu'arifat) and indicators (amarat); they are not real causes that positively affirm rulings. He then analyzes the definition of 'dalil': it gives knowledge of existence, not the existence itself. Therefore, whether hukm is the eternal speech or its effect, the proofs give us knowledge of the ruling. He further notes that knowledge can be either decisive (jazm) from the first three proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma') or preponderant (rajih) from qiyas. Finally, he addresses an objection: if hukm is taken as the eternal speech, it cannot be 'established' by proofs because the eternal is not subject to coming into existence. He resolves this by interpreting thubut al-hukm as thubut al-ilm bi-hukm (knowledge of the ruling). If hukm is the effect (obligation etc.), then the first three proofs establish it, but qiyas only reveals it, not creates it. This is a classic Hanafi position: qiyas is not a source that creates rulings but a method to discover rulings already present in the sources. The passage thus guards against misunderstanding proofs as causative agents.

Key Terms
دليل (dalil): That which gives knowledge of the existence or non-existence of something, not the existence itself.
علة حقيقية (illah haqiqiyya): A real cause that produces the ruling directly.
أمارة (amarah): A sign or indicator that leads to a preponderant assumption or knowledge of the thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the role of qiyas in relation to rulings?
A) It creates new rulings with certainty
B) It is a real cause that establishes rulings
C) It reveals or indicates a ruling that already exists
D) It is equal to the Quran in establishing rulings

Key Takeaway
Shari proofs are indicators (amarat) that give knowledge of rulings, not real causes that produce them; this distinction preserves the eternality of divine speech and properly limits the epistemic weight of qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Proving Multiple Inherent Attributes for a Single Essence
Philosophical argument proving multiple inherent attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the rational proof for multiple inherent attributes (a'rad dhatiyya) of a truly simple entity and identify the key logical steps.

Core Idea
A truly simple entity must have multiple inherent attributes—otherwise infinite regress or dependence on externals arises.

This passage presents a rational argument (dalil aqli) central to Hanafi usul al-fiqh, particularly in discussions on the attributes of causes (sifat al-illah). The proof shows that a single essence without parts can still possess multiple diverse attributes, each inhering due to the essence itself. Understanding this logical structure sharpens your ability to analyze the presuppositions of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Define the truly one (al-wahid al-haqiqi)
Clarify that it has no parts and cannot depend on external things.
2
Eliminate inherence due to a part
Since it has no parts, attributes cannot inhere due to a part.
3
Eliminate inherence due to something separate
A perfect essence cannot need external things for its attributes.
4
Eliminate infinite regress (tasalsul)
If each attribute inheres due to another attribute, an infinite chain results, which is impossible.
5
Conclude that at least one attribute inheres due to the essence itself
This establishes an inherent accident. For other attributes, the same reasoning forces them to be inherent as well, leading to multiplicity and diversity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ( وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا اسْتَدَلَّ عَلَى ثُبوتِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ الْمُتَنَوِّعَةِ لِشَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ بِأَنَّ الْوَاحِدَ الْحَقِيقِيَّ الَّذِي لَا كَثْرَةَ فِي ذَاتِهِ بِوَجْهٍ مِنَ الْوُجُوهِ يَتَّصِفُ بِصِفَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ، وَإِنْ كَانَ بَعْضُهَا حَقِيقِيًّا كَالْقُدْرَةِ وَبَعْضُهَا إِضَافِيًّا كَالْخَلْقِ وَبَعْضُهَا سَلْبِيًّا كَالتَّجَرُّدِ عَنِ الْمَادَّةِ. وَالْمُتَّصِفُ بِصِفَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مُتَّصِفٌ بِأَعْرَاضٍ ذَاتِيَّةٍ مُتَنَوِّعَةٍ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا شَيْءَ مِنْ تِلْكَ الصِّفَاتِ لَاحِقٌ لَهُ لِجُزْئِهِ لِعَدَمِ الْجُزْءِ لَهُ، وَلَا لِلْمُبَايِنِ لِامْتِنَاعِ احْتِيَاجِ الْوَاحِدِ الْحَقِيقِيِّ فِي صِفَاتِهِ إِلَى أَمْرٍ مُنْفَصِلٍ. وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَتَعَرَّضَ لِهَذَا أَيْضًا. وَحِينَئِذٍ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لُحُوقُ كُلٍّ مِنْهَا لِصِفَةٍ أُخْرَى فَيَلْزَمُ التَّسَلْسُلُ فِي الْمَبَادِئِ أَعْنِي الصِّفَاتِ الَّتِي كُلٌّ مِنْهَا مَبْدَأٌ لِصِفَةٍ أُخْرَى، وَهُوَ مُحَالٌ لِبُرْهَانٍ مَذْكُورٍ فِي الْكَلَامِ. أَوْ يَكُونُ بَعْضُهَا لِذَاتِهِ فَيَثْبُتُ عَرَضٌ ذَاتِيٌّ. وَحِينَئِذٍ فَالْبَعْضُ الْآخَرُ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِجُزْئِهِ لِمَا مَرَّ، فَهُوَ إِمَّا لِذَاتِهِ فَيَثْبُتُ عَرَضٌ ذَاتِيٌّ آخَرُ، وَهُوَ الْمَطْلُوبُ؛ أَوْ لِغَيْرِهِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْغَيْرُ مُبَايِنًا لِمَا مَرَّ، بَلْ يَكُونُ صِفَةً مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ. وَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَنْتَهِيَ إِلَى مَا يَكُونُ لُحُوقُهُ لِذَاتِهِ وَإِلَّا لَزِمَ التَّسَلْسُلُ فِي الْمَبَادِئِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَنْتَهِيَ إِلَى الْعَرَضِ الذَّاتِيِّ الْأَوَّلِ فَلَا يَلْزَمُ تَعَدُّدُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ. وَلَوْ سُلِّمَ فَاللَّازِمُ تَعَدُّدُهَا، وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَطْلُوبٍ؛ وَالْمَطْلُوبُ تَنَوُّعُهَا، وَهُوَ غَيْرُ لَازِمٍ. قُلْنَا: اللَّاحِقُ بِوَاسِطَةِ الْعَرَضِ الذَّاتِيِّ الْأَوَّلِ أَيْضًا عَرَضٌ ذَاتِيٌّ فَيَلْزَمُ التَّعَدُّدُ. وَالصِّفَاتُ الْمُتَعَدِّدَةُ فِي مَحَلٍّ وَاحِدٍ مُتَنَوِّعَةٌ لَا مَحَالَةَ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّ اخْتِلَافَ أَشْخَاصِ نَوْعٍ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحَلِّ. قَوْلُهُ (وَلِأَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ) عَطْفٌ عَلَى مَضْمُونِ الْكَلَامِ السَّابِقِ أَي: وَإِنْ كَانَ لِغَيْرِهِ فَهُوَ بَاطِلٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَسْتَلْزِمُ التَّسَلْسُلَ. وَلِأَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ اسْتِكْمَالُ الْوَاحِدِ الْحَقِيقِيِّ فِي صِفَاتِهِ بِالْغَيْرِ، وَهُوَ مُحَالٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يُوجِبُ النُّقْصَانَ فِي ذَاتِهِ وَالِاحْتِيَاجَ فِي كَمَالَاتِهِ. وَفِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْ أُرِيدَ اسْتِكْمَالُهُ بِالْأَمْرِ الْمُنْفَصِلِ فَظَاهِرٌ أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ لَازِمٍ لِجَوَازِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لُحُوقُ الْبَعْضِ الْآخَرِ لِصِفَةٍ. وَإِنْ أُرِيدَ أَعَمُّ مِنَ الْمُنْفَصِلِ وَالصِّفَةِ فَلَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّ احْتِيَاجَ بَعْضِ الصِّفَاتِ إِلَى الْبَعْضِ يُوجِبُ النُّقْصَانَ فِي الذَّاتِ، كَيْفَ وَالْخَلْقُ يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى الْعِلْمِ وَالْقُدْرَةِ وَالْإِرَادَةِ. وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ هَذَا مُخْتَصًّا بِمَا يَكُونُ الْغَيْرُ مُنْفَصِلًا، وَمَا سَبَقَ مُخْتَصًّا بِمَا يَكُونُ غَيْرَ مُنْفَصِلٍ، فَيَتِمُّ بِمَجْمُوعِهِمَا الْمَطْلُوبُ أَعْنِي إِثْبَاتَ عَرَضٍ ذَاتِيٍّ آخَرَ.
ترجمہ:۔ استدلال کیا ایک شئی کیلئے مختلف اعراض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے کہ بے شک وہ واحد حقیقی کہ جس کی ذات میں کثرت نہیں ہے وجوہ میں سے کسی وجہ سے بھی ۔ متصف ہے صفات کثیرہ کے ساتھ اگر چہ بعض صفات حقیقی ہیں جیسا کہ قدرت ہے اور بعض صفات اضافی ہیں جیسا کہ خلق ہے اور بعض صفات سلبی ہیں جیسا کہ مادہ سے خالی ہونا اور جو متصف ہے صفات کثیرہ کے ساتھ وہ مختلف اعراض ذاتیہ کے ساتھ متصف ہوتا ہے بوجہ ضروری ہونے اس بات کے کہ نہیں ہے کوئی شئی ان صفات میں سے لاحق اس کو اس کے جزو کی وجہ سے بوجہ اس کے جزو نہ ہونے کے اور نہ ہی امر مباین کی وجہ سے بوجہ ممتنع ہونے واحد حقیقی کے احتیاج کے اپنی صفات میں امر مباین کی طرف اور مناسب تھا کہ ذکر کرتے (مصنف ) اس کو بھی اور اس وقت یا تو ہو گا لاحق ہونا ان میں سے ہر ایک کا دوسری صفت کی وجہ سے پس لازم آمریکا تسلسل مبادی میں مراد لیتا ہوں میں وہ صفات کہ ان میں سے ہر صفت مبداء ہو دوسری صفت کا اور وہ محال ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو مذکور ہے کلام میں یا ہوگا (لحوق ) بعض صفات کا اس کی ذات کی وجہ سے پس ثابت ہو جائیگا عرض ذاتی اور اس وقت بعض دوسری صفات نہیں ہے جائز کہ لاحق ہوں وہ اس کو اس کے جز کی وجہ سے بیجہ اس کے جو گزر گیا یا وہ لاحق ہوں بالذات پس ثابت ہو جائیگا دوسرا عرض ذاتی اور وہ مطلوب ہے یا غیر کی وجہ سے اور نہیں ہے جائز کہ ہو وہ امر مباین بوجہ اس کے جو گزر گیا بلکہ ہو گا وہ غیر کوئی صفت اس کی صفات میں سے اور ضروری ہے یہ بات کہ منتہی ہو وہ یہاں تک کہ ہو جائے اس کا لاحق ہونا اس کی ذات کی وجہ سے وگرنہ لازم آئی کا تسلسل مبادی میں ۔ پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ جائز ہے کہ منتہی ہو جائے وہ پہلے عرض ذاتی تک پس نہیں لازم آئیگا اعراض ذاتیہ کا تعدد اور اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو پھر لازم آتا ہے ان (اعراض) کا تعدد اور وہ مطلوب نہیں ہے اور مطلوب ان (اعراض) کا تنوع ہے اور وہ لازم نہیں آتا ہم کہتے ہیں کہ لاحق ہونے والا پہلے عرض ذاتی کے واسطہ سے وہ بھی عرض ذاتی ہوگا پس لازم آئیگا تعد داور صفات متعددہ ایک محل میں ممنوع ہوتی ہیں لامحالہ بوجہ بدیہی ہونے اس بات کے کہ صفات میں سے
His statement: (And indeed we say: one deduces the proof of the existence of diverse inherent accidents for a single thing by the fact that the truly one who has no multiplicity in his essence in any way is qualified with many attributes, even if some of them are real like power, some relational like creation, and some negative like being free from matter. And whoever is qualified with many attributes is qualified with diverse inherent accidents, necessarily because none of those attributes inheres in him due to a part of him, since he has no part, nor due to something distinct, because it is impossible for the truly one to need a separate thing for his attributes. And it was appropriate to address this as well. Then, either each of them inheres due to another attribute, leading to an infinite regress in the principles — meaning the attributes each of which is a principle for another attribute — which is impossible by a proof mentioned in theology; or some of them inhere due to his essence, and then an inherent accident is established. Then, the other part cannot be due to his part for the reason given, so it is either due to his essence, establishing another inherent accident — and that is the desired proof; or due to another, and that other cannot be distinct for the reason given, but rather it is an attribute of his attributes. And it must end with what inheres due to his essence, otherwise an infinite regress in principles would follow. If it is said: It may end with the first inherent accident, so multiplicity of inherent accidents does not follow. And even if it is conceded, what follows is their multiplicity, which is not desired; the desired is their diversity, and that does not follow. We say: That which inheres by means of the first inherent accident is also an inherent accident, so multiplicity follows. And multiple attributes in a single locus are necessarily diverse, because the difference between individuals of one type of attributes is only by difference of locus. His statement (and because it necessitates) is conjoined with the meaning of the previous speech, i.e., and if it were due to another, it is invalid because it entails infinite regress. And because it necessitates the perfection of the truly one in his attributes by another, which is impossible because it causes deficiency in his essence and need in his perfections. And there is a consideration: because if what is meant is his perfection by a separate thing, then it is apparently not necessary, since it is possible for another part to inhere due to an attribute. And if what is meant is a general thing including both the separate and the attribute, then we do not accept that the need of some attributes for others causes deficiency in the essence, for how else would creation depend on knowledge, power, and will? And it is possible to make this specific to when the other is separate, and what preceded specific to when it is not separate, so by combining both, the desired goal is achieved, namely proving another inherent accident.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (dalil aqli) that a single real entity (al-wahid al-haqiqi) necessarily possesses multiple diverse inherent accidents (a'rad dhatiyya). The argument proceeds by elimination: the attributes of such an entity cannot inhere due to a part (since it has no parts), nor due to a separate external thing (since that would imply need and imperfection). They must either inhere due to another attribute (leading to infinite regress, which is impossible) or due to the essence itself. Thus, at least one attribute inheres due to the essence, establishing an inherent accident. For other attributes, if they were due to the same first accident, they would still be inherent accidents themselves, leading to multiplicity and diversity since multiple accidents in one locus are necessarily diverse. The commentator then considers an objection: does it prove diversity or just multiplicity? He replies that multiplicity in one locus implies diversity because the only difference within a single type of attribute is by locus. The text also addresses an argument that needing another for perfection implies deficiency, but the commentator refutes it by noting that some attributes (like creation) depend on others (knowledge, power, will) without causing deficiency in the essence. The Urdu translation reiterates the same argument in simpler terms.

Key Terms
العرض الذاتي (al-'arad al-dhati): An accident that inheres in a thing due to its essence, not due to an external cause or part.
الواحد الحقيقي (al-wahid al-haqiqi): That which has no multiplicity in its essence in any respect, i.e., absolutely simple.
التسلسل (al-tasalsul): An infinite regress of causes or principles, considered impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proof in this passage, why must a single real entity (al-wahid al-haqiqi) have multiple inherent accidents?
A) Because it has parts that each produce a different attribute.
B) Because it cannot derive attributes from parts or external things, and infinite regress is impossible, so attributes must be inherent and diverse.
C) Because it needs external things to complete its essence.
D) Because the attributes are all of the same type and thus do not require diversity.

Key Takeaway
A single real entity necessarily possesses multiple diverse inherent accidents, a key principle for analyzing attributes of causes in Hanafi usul.

Why Usuliyyun Focus on Verbal Speech
Answering why usul scholars discuss verbal speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why usul al-fiqh scholars discuss verbal speech rather than eternal speech, and apply this to delineate the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Rulings derive from commands and prohibitions in verbal speech, not from the eternal attribute.

A common question arises: if the Quran is eternal speech (kalam azali), why do usul scholars define and discuss verbal speech (kalam lafzi)? This lesson addresses that objection. The answer lies in the fact that legal rulings (ahkam) are established through commands (amr) and prohibitions (nahy), which are linguistic forms that exist only in verbal revelation. Thus, usul al-fiqh properly focuses on the revealed words, not the divine attribute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Recognize the question: If the Quran is eternal, why do usuliyyun discuss verbal speech instead of eternal speech?
The objection assumes usul al-fiqh should define its subject as the eternal attribute.
2
Distinguish kalam azali and kalam lafzi
Understand that eternal speech is an attribute of Allah, free from linguistic structure. Verbal speech is the revealed text in Arabic.
Kalam azali is not composed of letters or sounds; kalam lafzi is the Qur'an as we recite it.
3
Link rulings to commands and prohibitions
Rulings (ahkam) are derived from commands (amr) and prohibitions (nahy). These only occur in verbal speech because they are linguistic categories.
Eternal speech does not contain 'do' or 'do not' in a linguistic sense.
4
Conclude the scope of usul al-fiqh
Thus, usuliyyun must discuss verbal speech to establish how rulings are extracted from commands and prohibitions.
This defines the subject of usul al-fiqh as the verbal revelation (kalam lafzi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا ان سے سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ اصل قرآن تو ازلی ہے کلام لفظی تو کلام ازلی پر دال ہے تو اصولیوں کو ایسی تعریف کرنی چاہیئے جو کلام از لی اصلی پر صادق آئے حالانکہ اصولی کلام لفظی سے بحث کرتے ہیں؟ جواب:۔ اصولیین بحث کرتے ہیں اس اعتبار سے کہ احکام ثابت ہوں اور یہ احکام اس وقت ثابت ہونگے جب کلام میں امر نبی وغیرہ ہو اور یہ امر و نہی کلام لفظی میں ہوتے ہیں کیونکہ کلام ازلی میں امر و نہی نہیں پایا جاتا اس لئے اصولیین حضرات کلام لفظی سے بحث کرتے ہیں ۔
But a question has been answered. Question: It is that the original Quran is eternal; verbal speech indicates eternal speech. So the usuliyyun should give a definition that applies to the original eternal speech, whereas they discuss verbal speech? Answer: The usuliyyun discuss with the consideration that rulings are established, and these rulings are only established when the speech contains command, prohibition, etc. And these command and prohibition are present in verbal speech because in eternal speech there is no command or prohibition. Therefore, the usuliyyun discuss verbal speech.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: if the Quran is eternal speech, why do usul scholars define and discuss verbal speech? The answer is that legal rulings (ahkam) depend on commands and prohibitions, which only appear in verbal speech. Eternal speech (kalam azali) is free from such linguistic categories. Therefore, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the verbal speech (kalam lafzi) that contains commands and prohibitions, as these are the basis for deriving rulings. This clarifies the scope of usul al-fiqh: it deals with the revealed words, not the divine attribute.

Key Terms
اصولیین (usuliyyun): Scholars of usul al-fiqh.
امر و نہی (amr wa nahy): Command and prohibition, linguistic forms found in verbal speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because verbal speech is easier to understand.
B) Because rulings derive from commands and prohibitions, which only exist in verbal speech.
C) Because eternal speech cannot be translated.
D) Because verbal speech is the only form of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh focuses on verbal speech because it contains the commands and prohibitions from which rulings are derived.

Minimum Mahr Amount: Fourth Tafri'ah on Khas
Derivation of minimum mahr via qiyas on hand value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Hanafi school derives the minimum mahr from Quran 33:38 using qiyas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi minimum mahr is ten dirhams, derived by analogy from the hand value in theft — a text-based qiyas on the bud'a's substitution.

The amount of mahr is a key issue in Hanafi fiqh. While the Shafi'i school holds that any amount agreed upon is valid, the Hanafi school imposes a minimum of ten dirhams. This lesson explores the usul al-fiqh reasoning behind that ruling, focusing on the Quranic verse 'Qad 'alimna ma faradna' and the analogy (qiyas) used to derive the specific quantity. By understanding this derivation, you will see how a khas text and qiyas interact when no explicit quantity is given.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key verse and its textual category
Locate the Quranic verse 'Qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim fi azwajihim' (33:38). Identify that 'faradna' is interpreted as 'qaddarna' (We determined). This verse is classified as khas (specific) in Hanafi usul, indicating a specific determination for mahr.
The term 'faradna' is the operative word.
2
Determine the nature of the determination
Since there is consensus that there is no maximum limit for mahr, the determination must refer to a minimum. This is a logical inference (ta'lil) based on the absence of an upper bound.
This step narrows down the scope of the determination.
3
Apply qiyas to find the specific quantity
The Shariah set a value of ten dirhams for the cutting of a hand in theft (a hadith). Since marriage involves ownership of the vulva (bud'a), which is also a body part, the minimum substitute (mahr) should be analogous to the hand value. Thus, the minimum mahr is ten dirhams.
This is a qiyas on the illa of ownership of a body part.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i analogy
The Shafi'i school analogizes mahr to a price in a sale (qiyas on bay'), arguing that any capable price can be mahr. The Hanafi response is that marriage has its own independent textual basis (nass), so qiyas on sale is unnecessary – qiyas is only needed where there is no text.
This highlights a key usul principle: qiyas is subsidiary to nass.
5
Understand the usul principle applied
The overall derivation shows the Hanafi methodology: a khas text indicates a determination, but the specific quantity is found via qiyas on a closely analogous ruling. This demonstrates the interaction of textual categories and qiyas.
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاص کے حکم پر چوتھی تفریح قوله تعالى وقد علمنا ما فرضنا : یہاں سے خاص کے حکم پر چوتھی تفریح ہے اور اس سے پہلے بھی ایک مسئلہ سمجھیں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مہر کی مقدار شرعا متعین ہے یا نہیں؟ امام شافعی کے ہاں مہر کی مقدار شرعا متعین نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ زوجین خود جتنا مہر مقررکر لیں۔ اتنالازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور ان کے ہاں ہر وہ چیز جوشن (عوض) بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے وہ مہر بن سکتی ہے لیکن احناف کے ہاں زیادتی کے اعتبار سے تو مہر کی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے لیکن کمی کے اعتبار سے متعین ہے اور وہ ہے دس در ہم کہ اگر ہو دس درہم سے کم مقرر کیا گیا ہے تو دس درہم ہی لازم ہوں گے اس سے کم جائز نہیں ہوں گے۔ دلیل و تفریح:- قرآن پاک میں ارشاد باری ہے قد علمنا ما فرضنا عليهم في ازواجهم “ یہاں فرضنا بمعنی قدرنا ہے اور یہ خاص ہے اس سے اتنا پتہ چل رہا ہے کہ شریعت نے مہر کی مقدار کو مقرر کیا ہے اگر چہ یہ بیان نہیں کیا گیا کہ کتنا مہر مقرر ہے؟ اس کے بعد اب اس تقدیر میں دو احتمال ہیں کہ یہ تقدیر یکمی کے اعتبار سے ہے یا زیادتی کے اعتبار سے زیادتی کی کوئی حد نہیں ہے بالا جماع لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تقدیر کی کے اعتبار سے ہے اور وہ تقدیر ہے کتنی؟ اس کا بیان آیت میں نہیں ہے تو تقدیر قیاس کے ذریعہ سے کی گئی ہے کہ شریعت نے چوری میں قطع ید کے لیے دس دراہم کی شرط لگائی ہے تو گویا کہ شریعت نے آدمی کے ایک عضو یعنی ہاتھ کی قیمت دس دراہم رکھی ہے اور نکاح میں بھی زوج کو آدمی کے ایک عضو یعنی بضع پر ملک حاصل ہوتی ہے تو اس کا عوض ( مہر ) بھی کم از کم دس درہم ہونا چاہیے اس لیے ہم نے مقرر کر دیا کہ مہر کی کم از کم مقدار دس در اہم ہے۔ بخلاف شوافع کے وہ قیاس کرتے ہیں بیچ پر کہ جو چیز بیچ میں شمن بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے تو وہ مہر بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے لیکن اس کا ۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہاں نکاح کو بیچ پر قیاس کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ قیاس وہاں ہوتا ہے جہاں نص موجود نہ ہو حالانکہ یہاں پر نکاح کے جواز کے بارے میں مستقل نص موجود ہے۔ وَقَدْ أَوْرَدَ فَخْرُ الْإِسْلَامِ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فِى هَذَا الْفَصْلِ مَسَائِلَ أُخَرَ أَوْرَدْتُهَا فِي الزِّيَادَةِ عَلَى النَّصَّ فِي آخِرِ فَصْلِ النَّسْخِ إِلَّا مَسْأَلَتَيْنِ تَرَكْتُهُمَا بِالْكُلِّيَّةِ مَخَافَةَ التَّطْوِيلِ وَهُمَا مَسْأَلَتَا الْهَدْمِ وَالْقَطْعِ مَعَ الضَّمَانِ
Fourth Tafri'ah on the Ruling of Khas: The saying of Allah Ta'ala: 'We have known what We have prescribed' (al-Ahzab 33:38). From here is the fourth tafri'ah on the ruling of khas. Before this, understand one issue: Is the amount of mahr fixed by Shariah or not? According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the amount of mahr is not fixed by Shariah. Rather, whatever amount the spouses fix themselves becomes binding. And according to them, anything capable of being a substitute (i.e., a price) can be mahr. But according to the Hanafis, the amount of mahr is not fixed with respect to excess, but it is fixed with respect to deficiency, and that is ten dirhams: if less than ten dirhams is fixed, then ten dirhams become binding; less than that is not permissible. Proof and tafri'ah: In the Holy Quran, Allah says: 'Qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim fi azwajihim' (We have known what We have prescribed for them concerning their wives). Here, 'faradna' means 'qaddarna' (We determined). And this is khas (specific). From this, it is understood that the Shariah has determined the amount of mahr, although it is not stated how much is determined. Then, there are two possibilities regarding this determination: either this determination is with respect to deficiency or with respect to excess. There is no upper limit by consensus, so it becomes clear that this determination is with respect to deficiency. But what amount? It is not stated in the verse. So the determination is made through qiyas (analogy): that the Shariah has stipulated ten dirhams for the cutting of the hand (in theft). So it is as if the Shariah valued one limb of a person, i.e., the hand, at ten dirhams. In marriage, the husband also gains ownership of a limb of the person, i.e., the vulva (bud'a), so its substitute (mahr) should also be at least ten dirhams. Therefore, we have determined that the minimum amount of mahr is ten dirhams. Contrary to the Shafi'is, they make qiyas on sale: whatever is capable of being a price in sale is capable of being mahr. But its answer is that here there is no need for qiyas on sale because qiyas is applied where there is no text (nass), yet here there is an independent text concerning the validity of marriage. And Fakhr al-Islam, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated in this chapter other issues which I have narrated in the addition to the nass at the end of the chapter on naskh, except two issues which I have left out entirely for fear of prolongation, and they are the issues of destruction (al-hadm) and cutting (al-qat') with guarantee (al-daman).
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is the fourth tafri'ah on the ruling of khas, dealing with the minimum amount of mahr. It begins by contrasting the Shafi'i and Hanafi positions: Shafi'is hold that no minimum is set (anything of value can be mahr), while Hanafis set a minimum of ten dirhams, though no maximum. The proof is from the Quranic verse 'Qad 'alimna ma faradna' where 'faradna' means 'determined'. This verse is khas, indicating that the Shariah determined a quantity, but it is not explicit. Since no maximum is agreed upon by consensus, the determination must be for the minimum. The minimum is derived through qiyas: the value of a hand in theft (ten dirhams) is analogically applied to the ownership of the vulva (bud'a) in marriage, as both involve a body part. Thus, the minimum substitute for such ownership is ten dirhams. The Hanafis reject the Shafi'i analogy to sale because marriage has its own independent textual basis (nass), making qiyas unnecessary—a key usul point: qiyas is only used where there is no text. The passage ends with a note by the commentator (Fakhr al-Islam) that he included other related issues in the chapter on naskh except two (al-hadm and al-qat' ma'a al-daman) which he omitted for brevity.

Key Terms
فرضنا (faradna): In this verse, interpreted by Hanafis as 'qaddarna' (We determined), indicating a fixed quantity.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used here to derive the minimum mahr from the hand value in theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Direct Quranic statement specifying ten dirhams.
B) Analogy (qiyas) on the value of a hand in theft (cutting of hand).
C) Ijma of the companions.
D) The sunnah of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams is derived via qiyas from the hand value in theft, using a text (khas) from Quran 33:38.

Prayer Inside the Kaaba: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute over the validity of fard prayer inside the Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of qiyas to extend a ruling from a narrated action (hikayat al-fi'l) and evaluate the Shafi'i objection based on restricting the action to its specific case.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends the Prophet's action from nafl to fard when the 'illah (facing qibla) is identical.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the scope of the Prophet's actions. The disagreement centers on whether a reported action (hikayat al-fi'l) can be extended via qiyas to cover other similar cases. Understanding this debate clarifies the Hanafi method of analogical reasoning and the role of 'illah in applying the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine the exact legal issue: Is fard prayer inside the Kaaba permissible?
This issue arises because some argue that facing the entire Kaaba is required for fard.
2
State each school's position and its proof
Hanafis: permissible, using qiyas from the Prophet's nafl prayer inside the Kaaba. Shafi'is: not permissible, restricting the action to nafl only.
Pay attention to the proof structure: the Hanafi proof is qiyas, the Shafi'i proof is restriction (takhsis) of the action.
3
Analyze the Hanafi qiyas
Identify the elements: asl (nafl prayer inside Kaaba, permissible by Prophet's action), far' (fard prayer inside Kaaba), illah (equality in requirement of facing qibla), and hukm (permissibility).
The illah is jaliyyah (clear) because both share the same essential requirement.
4
Compare the usul principles
Hanafis use qiyas to extend the ruling; Shafi'is restrict the prophetic action to its specific context. Understand how the difference in principle leads to different rulings.
This comparison highlights the role of qiyas in Hanafi usul as a primary method of istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے نفل مراد ہے ۔ اب امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ جواز نفلی نماز کیساتھ ہی خاص ہے فرض نماز کعبہ میں جائز نہیں ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کعبہ میں نماز پڑھنے سے کعبہ کے بعض اجزاء کو استند بار ( پیٹھ کرنا ) لازم آئے گا اور وہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ ہاں چونکہ نفل نماز کے بارہ میں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل کی حکایت منقول ہے اس لیے نفل نماز جائز ہوگی فرض نماز اپنی حالت پر رہے گی۔ لیکن احناف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں نماز کی تمام حالتیں یعنی فرض اور نفل اس بات میں برابر نہیں کہ حالت اختیار میں استقبال قبلہ ضروری ہے کسی نماز میں بھی استند بار درست نہیں ہے تو جب نبی اکر ملے سے نماز کی ایک حالت میں بعض اجزاء قبلہ کا استقبال نہ کرنے کا جواز ثابت ہو گیا تو باقی حالتوں میں بھی قیاس کے ذریعے جواز ثابت ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اس امر میں دونوں حالتیں برابر ہیں تو ایک صورت (نفل) میں جواز ثابت ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل سے تو دوسری صورت (فرائض ) میں ثابت ہو جائیگا قیاس ہے۔
By 'nafl' is meant. Now Imam Shafi'i says that this permissibility is specific to nafl prayer; fard prayer is not permissible in the Kaaba. The reason is that praying inside the Kaaba necessitates turning one's back towards some parts of the Kaaba, which is not correct. Yes, because the narration of the Prophet's action regarding nafl prayer is transmitted, so nafl prayer will be permissible; fard prayer remains on its original ruling. But the Hanafis say that all states of prayer, i.e., fard and nafl, are equal in that facing the qibla is necessary in the state of choice; turning one's back is not correct in any prayer. So when the Prophet's action established the permissibility of not facing some parts of the qibla in one state of prayer, then in the remaining states it is also established by qiyas, because in this matter both states are equal. So in one case (nafl) permissibility is established by the Prophet's action, then in the other case (fara'id) it is established by qiyas.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the validity of prayer inside the Kaaba. Shafi'i argues that only nafl prayer is permissible because the Prophet's reported action of praying inside the Kaaba specifically applies to nafl; for fard prayer, turning one's back to parts of the Kaaba is not allowed. Hanafis respond by stating that both fard and nafl are equal with regard to the requirement of facing the qibla. Since the Prophet's action demonstrated that in one case (nafl) it is permissible to not face all parts of the Kaaba, by analogy (qiyas) the same applies to fard prayer. The Hanafi position is that qiyas extends the ruling from the reported case to similar cases.

Key Terms
حكاية الفعل (Hikayat al-Fi'l): Narration of an action of the Prophet, used as a proof in fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, why is fard prayer inside the Kaaba valid?
A) Because the Prophet did it
B) Because qiyas extends the permissibility from nafl to fard
C) Because it is recommended
D) Because there is no requirement to face the qibla inside

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (hikayat al-fi'l) can be extended to similar cases via qiyas when the 'illah (effective cause) is common.

Pages p. 637 · Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
